The plumbing inspector shall keep on file in his office three (3) copies of the
state plumbing code, which shall be available for inspection. (1967 Code §
14.106; amd. 2010 Code)
4-1A-2: PERMIT REQUIRED; APPLICATION:
No plumbing shall be installed in any place in the city unless a permit
therefor is first obtained. Applications for such permits shall be made to the
clerk and shall state thereon the name of the person or contractor intended to
have charge of the installation, and the nature and extent of the proposed
installation. (1967 Code § 14.101)
4-1A-3: PERMIT FEE:
The fee for a permit shall be one dollar fifty cents ($1.50) for each fixture
included in the system. Bathtubs, lavatories, closets, sinks, laundry tubs,
drinking fountains, shower receptacles, urinals, sinks, soda fountains and
traps shall be considered fixtures. (1967 Code § 14.102)
4-1A-4: EXPOSURE FOR INSPECTION:
In all buildings hereafter erected, both public and private, and in all
buildings already built or erected wherein any plumbing is hereafter installed
or wherein any sewer or connection pipe shall be hereafter repaired or changed,
except for minor repairs, on the sewer side of the trap, the drain, soil,
rainwater and other pipe or pipes directly or indirectly connected into any
drain, soil or waste pipe, and all traps, shall be exposed for view for
inspection and test by the plumbing inspector, and shall not be covered until
such test is made. (1967 Code § 14.103)
4-1A-5: ENFORCING OFFICER:
The plumbing inspector shall enforce the provisions of the state plumbing code
in the city. (1967 Code § 14.105)
4-1A-6: STANDARDS:
All work done on any plumbing system shall be performed in an efficient and
workmanlike manner. (1967 Code § 14.108)
4-1A-7: PENALTY:
Any person violating any of the provisions of this article, or continuing to
work in violation of a stop order issued by the plumbing inspector 1 , shall be
subject to penalty under the provisions of section
1-4-1 of this code for each offense, and a separate offense shall be deemed
committed on each day during or on which a violation occurs or continues. (1967
Code § 14.109; amd. 1977 Code)
 
Notes
1 1. See subsection
  1-11-3C2 of this code.
ARTICLE B.  ELECTRICAL CODE
SECTION:
4-1B-1: Definition
4-1B-2: Rules And Regulations Adopted
4-1B-3: Permit Required; Application
4-1B-4: Certificate Of Approval
4-1B-5: Penalty
4-1B-1: DEFINITION:
The term "electrical equipment", as used in this article, shall be construed to
mean and include conductors and equipment installed for the utilization of
electricity supplied for light, heat or power, but does not include radio
apparatus or equipment for the wireless reception of sounds and signals, nor
ordinary household equipment or appliances such as toasters, vacuum cleaners,
and washing machines, and does not include apparatus, conductors and other
equipment installed for and by the public utilities, including common carriers,
which are under the jurisdiction of the Illinois commerce commission for use in
their operation as public utilities. (1967 Code § 17.001)
4-1B-2: RULES AND REGULATIONS ADOPTED:
The following are hereby adopted as safe and practical standards for the
installation, alteration and use of electrical equipment in the city:
   A.   The rules and regulations of the National Board of Fire Underwriters,
as contained in the code known as the national electrical code, and as approved
by the American Standards Association, as last published.
   B.   The rules and regulations regarding the installation, alteration and
use of electrical equipment as adopted by the electricity supply company now
supplying the city, as last published and filed with the Illinois commerce
commission, a copy of said code and the last mentioned rules and regulations
being now on file in the office of the clerk and of the electrical inspector.
(1967 Code § 17.002)
4-1B-3: PERMIT REQUIRED; APPLICATION:
The following are hereby adopted as reasonable rules and regulations governing
the issuance of permits for electrical installations or alterations:
   A.   It shall be unlawful to install or alter any electrical equipment or
wiring without having first secured a permit therefor.
   B.   Applications for such permits shall be made in writing to the clerk,
and shall be referred by him to the electrical inspector.
   C.   Each application shall contain the name of the owner of the premises to
be served, the name of the contractor doing the work and the nature of the work
to be done. Where the work consists of new installations or extensive repairs
or alterations, plans and specifications of the work shall accompany the
application. (1967 Code § 17.003)
4-1B-4: CERTIFICATE OF APPROVAL:
The electrical inspector shall issue a certificate of approval after each
inspection in which the wiring or apparatus is found to be in compliance with
the terms of this article and with the rules adopted hereby.
It shall be unlawful to use or to turn on power into any wires or apparatus
hereinafter installed for which such certificate has not been issued because
the permit was not secured for installation or because the work was not
completed according to the provisions of this article. (1967 Code § 17.005)
4-1B-5: PENALTY:
Any person violating any provisions of this article shall be subject to penalty
under the provisions of section
1-4-1 of this code for each offense, and a separate offense shall be deemed
committed on each day during or on which a violation occurs or continues. (1977
Code)
CHAPTER 2
BUILDING PERMITS; GENERAL BUILDING REGULATIONS
SECTION:
4-2-1: Permit Required
4-2-2: Application For Permit
4-2-3: Approval Of Plans
4-2-4: Permit Fees
4-2-5: Variations
4-2-6: Bond For Contractor Excavations
4-2-7: Enforcement Of Provisions
4-2-8: Term Of Permit
4-2-9: Stop Work Order
4-2-10: Interpretation
4-2-11: Penalty
4-2-1: PERMIT REQUIRED:
It shall be unlawful to construct any building or structure, other than a
fence, in the city where the cost of such construction exceeds one hundred
dollars ($100.00), or to alter or remodel any building or structure so as to
change the bearing walls, beams, supports or the roof thereof, without having
first secured a permit therefor. (1967 Code § 13.101)
4-2-2: APPLICATION FOR PERMIT:
Applications for such permits shall be made to the building inspector and shall
be accompanied by plans and specifications in duplicate, showing the work to be
done; such plans shall be verified by the signature of either the owner of the
premises or by the architect or contractor in charge of operations. (1967 Code
§ 13.103)
4-2-3: APPROVAL OF PLANS:
Such applications with plans shall be referred to the building inspector, who
shall examine the same to determine whether the proposed alterations will
comply with the ordinance provisions relating thereto. Upon approval, one set
of plans shall be returned by the building inspector. No permit shall be issued
except after approval of the plans and payment of the fee provided herein.
(1967 Code § 13.104)
4-2-4: PERMIT FEES:
The fees for such permits shall be as follows:
Building permit fee schedule:
$35.00 minimum for the first $5,000.00 in value, then $1.00 for $1,000.00 in
value.
The above fees are for the following permits:
Alterations.
Apartments, per apartment unit.
Dwelling house, 1 story or 11/2 stories.
1 or 2 car garage.
Other buildings, including commercial. (Ord., 4-10-2012, eff. 5-1-2012)
4-2-5: VARIATIONS:
It shall be unlawful to vary from the approved plans and specifications
deposited with and approved by the city council unless amended plans and
specifications showing such proposed alteration or variation are first filed
with the city council and approved thereby; if such variation involves an
increase in the total cost of the work, a statement to that effect shall be
made and the necessary additional fee shall be paid. (1967 Code § 13.106)
4-2-6: BOND FOR CONTRACTOR EXCAVATIONS:
It shall be unlawful to commence work on any excavation, or on any construction
work in the city involving driving or hauling machinery, trucks or equipment
over any parkway or sidewalk area, or involving excavating or leveling of any
parkway or sidewalk area unless the person doing such work shall first have
filed with the city council a bond, with corporate surety, conditioned to
indemnify the city for any damage done to any city property, including any
curb, pavement, cable, pipe, shutoff box or other equipment, in the course of
such work.
Where the work contemplated includes the making of any excavation for any
structure or foundation, the bond shall also be conditioned that the building
or structure contemplated shall be completed within one year from the date of
commencement of work or the excavation refilled and the surface restored to its
original condition.
Such bond shall be in the principal amount of five thousand dollars
($5,000.00), payable to the city, in the event of any breach of the conditions
of such bond. (1967 Code § 13.107)
4-2-7: ENFORCEMENT OF PROVISIONS:
It shall be the duty of the building inspector and any lawfully appointed
deputies to enforce the provisions of this title. The building inspector is
hereby empowered to make such inspections as may be necessary to see to the
enforcement of these provisions, and to make any tests or examinations of
materials or methods to be used, for the purpose of seeing if they comply with
the provisions of this title. (1967 Code § 13.108)
4-2-8: TERM OF PERMIT:
No building permit shall be valid for a period of more than one year from the
date of issuance. (1967 Code § 13.109)
4-2-9: STOP WORK ORDER 1 :
The building inspector, or such other person as may be authorized by the city
council, may order work stopped whenever any construction, alteration or repair
work is being done in violation of any provision of this title. Such stop
order, when oral, shall be followed by a written stop order within twenty four
(24) hours. It shall be unlawful to continue work in violation of a stop order
until such order has been revoked by the person issuing it or by the city
council. (1967 Code § 13.110)
 
Notes
1 1. See also subsection
  1-11-1E of this code.
4-2-10: INTERPRETATION:
Whenever in the building regulations it is provided that anything must be done
to the approval of or subject to the direction of the building inspector or any
other officer of the city, this shall be construed to give such officer only
the discretion of determining whether or not there has been compliance with the
rules and standards established by ordinance, and no such provisions shall be
construed as giving any officer discretionary powers as to what such
regulations or standards shall be, or power to require conditions not
prescribed by ordinance, or to enforce ordinance provisions in an arbitrary or
discriminatory manner. (1967 Code § 13.111)
4-2-11: PENALTY:
Any person violating any provision of this chapter shall be subject to penalty
under the provisions of section
1-4-1 of this code for each offense, and a separate offense shall be deemed
committed on each day during or on which a violation occurs or continues. (1977
Code)
CHAPTER 3
NUMBERING BUILDINGS
SECTION:
4-3-1: Numbering Required
4-3-2: Plan
4-3-3: Chart
4-3-4: Owner And Occupant To Number; Specifications
4-3-1: NUMBERING REQUIRED:
All lots, buildings and structures in the city shall be numbered in accordance
with the plan described in section
4-3-2 of this chapter. (1967 Code § 10.501)
4-3-2: PLAN:
   A.   Jefferson Street shall be the base or dividing line for numbering
houses on all streets running north and south, and Washington Street shall be
the base or dividing line for all streets running east and west. All streets
running north and south and crossing and being north of Jefferson Street shall
be designated by the prefix "North"; and the portion of all streets crossing
and being south of Jefferson Street shall be designated by the prefix "South".
All streets running east and west and crossing and being east of Washington
Street shall be designated by the prefix "East", and that portion of the
streets lying west of Washington Street shall be designated by the prefix
"West". (1967 Code § 10.502)
   B.   All streets running north and south and being north or south of but not
crossing Jefferson Street shall not be designated by the prefix "North" or
"South", and all streets running east and west and being east or west of but
not crossing Washington Street shall not be designated by the prefix "East" or
"West", and said streets shall be numbered in the same manner and in accordance
with the same system of numbering as set forth in subsection C of this section.
The provisions of this subsection shall in no way change, modify or amend the
provisions of this chapter for the numbering of houses on streets which cross
Jefferson Street or Washington Street, and all such streets so crossing said
base or dividing lines shall continue to be designated by the prefixes "North",
"South", "East" and "West". (Ord., 6-24-1975)
   C.   The first number on each side of Jefferson Street shall be one hundred
(100) and progress north and south therefrom at the rate of one hundred (100)
numbers to each block. The first number on each side of Washington Street shall
be one hundred (100) and progress east and west therefrom at the rate of one
hundred (100) numbers to each block. The odd numbers shall be used upon the
east side of all streets running north and south and upon the north side of all
streets running east and west. Even numbers shall be used on the west side of
all streets running north and south and upon the south side of all the streets
running east and west. (1967 Code § 10.503)
4-3-3: CHART:
The city clerk shall keep a chart showing the proper street number of every lot
in the city, or part lot, allotting one number to each twenty five feet (25'),
which chart shall be open for inspection by anyone interested therein. (1967
Code § 10.504)
4-3-4: OWNER AND OCCUPANT TO NUMBER; SPECIFICATIONS:
It shall be the duty of the owner and occupant of every house in the city to
have placed thereon, in a place visible from the street, figures showing the
number of that house. (1967 Code § 10.505)
The figures of each number shall not be less than two and one- half inches (21/
2") in height. Each figure shall be legible and placed in a conspicuous
position on the front side or above the front door of each building. (1967 Code
§ 10.505; amd. 1977 Code)
Any person failing to so number any house owned or occupied by him thirty (30)
days after receiving notice from the city clerk shall be fined one dollar
($1.00) for each day on which the failure continues. (1967 Code § 10.505)
CHAPTER 4
BILLBOARDS
SECTION:
4-4-1: Definition
4-4-2: Permit Required; Fee
4-4-3: Application For Permit
4-4-4: Specifications And Restrictions
4-4-5: Nuisances
4-4-6: Enforcement
4-4-7: Penalty
4-4-1: DEFINITION:
The term "billboard" is hereby defined to mean and, for the purpose of this
chapter, shall be construed to mean any signboard or similar structure, the
sole or primary purpose of which is to be used for the display of
advertisements or notices. (1967 Code § 13.601)
4-4-2: PERMIT REQUIRED; FEE:
It shall be unlawful to construct a billboard within the city without having
first secured a permit therefor from the city council; provided, that this
section shall not be construed to require a permit for the construction of a
billboard or signboard, other than a roof sign, the total display area of which
does not exceed fifteen (15) square feet; and provided, that no permit issued
hereunder shall be construed to authorize the construction of or maintenance of
a billboard which extends over any public street, alley or sidewalk or other
public place 1 . The fee for a permit to construct any such billboard shall be
ten dollars ($10.00). (1967 Code § 13.602; amd. 2010 Code)
 
Notes
1 1. See title 8, chapter 3 of this code for signs over public ways.
4-4-3: APPLICATION FOR PERMIT:
Applications for such permits shall be made in writing to the clerk. Each
application shall state thereon the name of the owner of the premises, the name
of the person or corporation constructing the billboard and specifications
showing the size, material and manner of construction of the billboard. (1967
Code § 13.603)
4-4-4: SPECIFICATIONS AND RESTRICTIONS:
   A.   Wind Pressure: Every billboard shall be firmly and solidly constructed
so as to be able to bear a wind pressure of at least thirty (30) pounds per
square foot of area; provided, that billboards which are placed upon roofs must
be so constructed as to be able to withstand a lateral wind pressure of forty
(40) pounds per square inch. (1967 Code § 13.604)
   B.   Fire Escapes: It shall be unlawful to erect or maintain any billboard
in such a position as to obstruct any fire escape or any window or door leading
thereto, and no billboard shall be fastened to any fire escape. (1967 Code §
13.605)
   C.   Height Above Ground: Every billboard must be so constructed as to leave
an open space of at least two and one-half feet (21/2') between the bottom of
the display area and the ground. This open area may be filled with lattice work
or other ornamental design which does not close off more than two- thirds (2/3)
of any square foot of such open area. Billboards constructed on property on
which there is a properly established building line must be built entirely in
back of this building line, and no permit shall be issued for the construction
of any billboard upon any lot which is subject to a proper building line
restriction, if the billboard is to be constructed in violation of the building
line restriction. (1967 Code § 13.606)
   D.   Fireproof Construction: It shall be unlawful to construct any billboard
of over fifteen (15) square feet in area anywhere in the fire limits unless the
face of such billboard is constructed of noncombustible material. (1967 Code §
13.607)
   E.   Roof Signs: It shall be unlawful to construct any billboard on the roof
of any building or structure of any but incombustible materials. All such roof
signs or billboards must be so constructed so that there is at least four feet
(4') of space between the billboard or signboard and the edge of the roof at
all sides and ends. It shall be unlawful to construct any roof sign or
billboard on the roof of any building which is unable to withstand the
additional weight and wind pressure imposed by such construction. All roof
signs and billboards which are constructed entirely of fireproof materials
shall be so constructed and braced that the supports of such signs or
billboards shall bear directly on the masonry walls of such buildings or upon
the steel girders which are supported by the masonry walls.
The metal supports and parts of every roof sign shall be thoroughly and
properly painted at least once each two (2) years, unless they are galvanized
or otherwise adequately protected against rust and corrosion. (1967 Code §
13.608)
   F.   Billboards Near Buildings: It shall be unlawful to construct any
billboard, a majority of the display area of which is within four feet (4') of
any building, unless such billboard is constructed of noncombustible material.
(1967 Code § 13.609)
   G.   Illuminated Billboards: The wiring of illuminated billboards and
signboards must comply with the provisions of the ordinances relating to
electrical wiring 1 . (1967 Code § 13.610)
 
Notes
1 1. See chapter 1, article B of this title.
4-4-5: NUISANCES:
Any billboard or signboard which is dangerous because of insecure construction
or fastening with resultant danger of falling, or because it is an extreme fire
hazard and in fact a nuisance, is hereby declared to be a nuisance and may be
abated as such. (1967 Code § 13.611)
4-4-6: ENFORCEMENT:
It shall be the duty of the building inspector to enforce the provisions of
this chapter, and he is hereby authorized to do so. (1967 Code § 13.612)
4-4-7: PENALTY:
Any person violating any provision of this chapter shall be subject to penalty
under the provisions of section
1-4-1 of this code for each offense, and a separate offense shall be deemed
committed on each day during or on which a violation occurs or continues. (1977
Code)
CHAPTER 5
DANGEROUS BUILDINGS
SECTION:
4-5-1: Definition; Nuisance Declared
4-5-2: Prohibition
4-5-3: Abatement
4-5-4: Buildings Within Fire Limits
4-5-5: Penalty
4-5-1: DEFINITION; NUISANCE DECLARED:
The term "dangerous buildings", as used in this chapter, is hereby defined to
mean and include:
   A.   Any building, shed, fence or other manmade structure which is dangerous
to the public health because of its condition, and which may cause or aid in
the spread of disease, or injury to the health of the occupants of it or
neighboring structures.
   B.   Any building, shed, fence or other manmade structure which, because of
faulty construction, age, lack of proper repair or any other cause, is
especially liable to fire and constitutes or creates a fire hazard.
   C.   Any building, shed, fence or other manmade structure which, by reason
of faulty construction or other cause, is liable to cause injury or damage by
collapsing or by a collapse or fall of any part of such structure.
   D.   Any building, shed, fence or other manmade structure which, because of
its condition or because of lack of doors or windows, is available to and
frequented by malefactors or disorderly persons who are not lawful occupants of
such structure.
Any such dangerous building in the city is hereby declared to be a nuisance.
(1967 Code § 13.301)
4-5-2: PROHIBITION:
It shall be unlawful to maintain or permit the existence of any dangerous
building in the city; and it shall be unlawful for the owner, occupant or
person in custody of any dangerous building to permit the same to remain in a
dangerous condition, or to occupy such building or permit it to be occupied
while it is or remains in a dangerous condition. (1967 Code § 13.302)
4-5-3: ABATEMENT:
Whenever the building inspector, the director of public works or the county
health officer shall be of the opinion that any building or structure in the
city is a dangerous building, he shall file a written statement to this effect
with the city clerk. The clerk shall, upon order of the city council, cause
written notice to be served upon the owner thereof, and upon the occupant
thereof, if any, by registered mail or by personal service. Such notice shall
state that the building has been declared to be in a dangerous condition, and
that such dangerous condition must be removed or remedied by repairing or
altering the building or by demolishing it, and that the condition must be
remedied. Such notice may be in the following terms: (1967 Code § 13.303; amd.
2010 Code)
To                  (owner-occupant of premises) of the premises known and
described as                         .
You are hereby notified that (describe building) on the premises above
mentioned has been condemned as a nuisance and a dangerous building after
inspection by the Building Inspector.
The causes for this decision are (here insert the facts as to the dangerous
condition).
You must remedy this condition or demolish the building immediately, or the
City will proceed to do so.
If the person receiving the notice has not complied therewith or taken an
appeal from the determination of the officer or employee finding that a
dangerous building exists, within ten (10) days from the time when this notice
is served upon such person by personal service or registered mail, the building
inspector may, upon orders of the city council, proceed to remedy the condition
or demolish the dangerous building. (1967 Code § 13.303)
4-5-4: BUILDINGS WITHIN FIRE LIMITS:
Any frame building or structure within the fire limits of the city which has or
may be damaged by fire, decay or other causes to the extent of fifty percent
(50%) of its fair market value at the time of damage, shall be torn down and
removed, or rebuilt with nonflammable walls.
Upon written notice by the building inspector, the county health officer or the
director of public works to the effect that such building has been so damaged,
filed with the city clerk, the clerk shall notify the city council of the
receipt of such notice. (1967 Code § 13.304; amd. 1977 Code; 2010 Code)
The city council shall then appoint three (3) persons to determine whether or
not such building or structure has been damaged to the extent of fifty percent
(50%) of its fair market value at the time of damage.
A copy of the notice of the appointment of this board of three (3) persons to
determine the damage shall be served upon the owner of the premises by personal
service or by registered mail at his last known address. Such notice shall be
in substantially the following form:
To                            
You are hereby notified that                          has determined that the
building owned by you at                            located within the fire
limits of the City has been damaged by fire, decay or otherwise to the extent
of fifty percent (50%) of its fair market value at the time of damage, and that
a board of three (3) persons has been appointed to verify this finding, which
board will hold its first meeting in the City Hall on the                day of
               at the hour of              o'clock, at which time it will
determine whether or not this finding is correct.
If this finding is verified by the board, you must tear down and remove the
said building, or rebuild it with nonflammable walls.
If this finding is verified by the board of three (3) members, and it
determines that the building in question has been damaged to the extent of
fifty percent (50%) of its fair market value at the time of damage, it shall be
the duty of the owner to tear down and remove the said building within twenty
(20) days after the finding of such board, or to remodel it to comply with the
requirements of new buildings in the fire limits, and it shall be unlawful to
occupy or permit the occupancy of such building after such finding until it is
so remodeled. (1967 Code § 13.304; amd. 1977 Code)
4-5-5: PENALTY:
Any person violating any provision of this chapter, or permitting any dangerous
building, or any building or structure to remain in a dangerous condition, or
to remain in the fire limits without remodeling as provided in this chapter,
after it has been damaged to the extent of fifty percent (50%) of its fair
market value at the time of damage, shall be subject to penalty under the
provisions of section
1-4-1 of this code for each offense, and a separate offense shall be deemed
committed on each day during or on which a violation occurs or continues. (1967
Code § 13.305; amd. 1977 Code)
CHAPTER 6
RENTAL HOUSING NOTIFICATION AND INSPECTION PROGRAM
SECTION:
4-6-1: Mandatory Rental Housing Notification And Inspection Program
4-6-1: MANDATORY RENTAL HOUSING NOTIFICATION AND INSPECTION PROGRAM:
   A.   Inspection Required; Definitions:
      1.   Inspection Of Property: No person shall lease, let, or otherwise
allow, the use of any property as a rental dwelling within the city unless that
property has been inspected by the building inspector.
      2.   Inspections Prior To Enactment: Inspections made prior to the
enactment of this section shall be considered an inspection under this section.
      3.   Definitions:
    BUILDING INSPECTOR: The building inspector of the city or any of his/her
employees or agents.
   OWNER: Any person or legal entity who has a full or partial ownership
interest in a rental dwelling either by deed, including life estate deed, or
land installment contract (contract for deed).
   RENTAL DWELLING: A unit of residential real estate not occupied by an owner
which is leased, let or otherwise allowed to be used for residential purposes
in exchange for consideration. Separate dwelling units of the same building
shall be considered separate rental dwellings. There is a rebuttable
presumption that residential real estate that is not occupied by an owner is a
rental dwelling. This presumption may be rebutted by clear and convincing
evidence.
   B.   Inspections Authorized:
      1.   The building inspector is hereby authorized and obligated to conduct
inspections of any and all rental dwellings, or units thereof, within the city
to determine compliance with the standards and regulations set forth in this
code.
      2.   The building inspector is hereby authorized to enter, examine and
survey all rental dwellings within the city. All inspections shall occur at
reasonable hours except in emergency situations where the life, health, and/or
safety of any individual is threatened.
   C.   Frequency, Access For And Notice Of Inspection:
      1.   All rental dwellings shall be inspected by the building inspector
upon becoming a rental dwelling and once every five (5) years thereafter.
Additionally, a rental dwelling shall be inspected between three (3) and five
(5) years from the last inspection if the rental unit has a new tenant since
the last inspection. Inspections may occur more frequently, provided there is:
         a.   Reasonable suspicion to believe that there exists conditions
which present a threat to the health, safety, welfare or general comfort of the
resident(s) of such rental dwelling; or
         b.   A complaint lodged by the resident(s) of the rental dwelling to
be inspected; or
         c.   A request made by a prospective resident accompanied by the
consent of the owner (or owner's agent) of the rental dwelling to be inspected;
or
         d.   A request made by the owner or owner's agent.
      2.   Every owner or owner's agent of any rental dwelling shall provide
access to such rental dwelling, or any unit thereof, to the building inspector
for purposes of inspecting the rental dwelling or unit thereof for compliance
with all applicable standards and regulations set forth in this code. Either
the owner, the owner's agent, or the occupant shall accompany the inspector
during the inspection.
      3.   Notice shall be given to the owner or the owner's agent and the
occupant of the rental dwelling, or unit thereof, at least one hundred twenty
(120) hours in advance of such inspection except in those situations described
in subsections C1a, C1b, and C1d of this section.
      4.   Notice of inspection shall be provided to both the owner or owner's
agent and occupant and may consist of a letter sent by first class mail,
personal service, telephone call or, for occupants only, the posting of a door
hanger upon the doorknob of the rental dwelling. The form of notice shall be at
the city's sole discretion; provided, however, the form used substantially
achieves the purpose of this "notice" requirement. Where a rental dwelling is
occupied by more than one person, notice to one occupant shall be deemed notice
to all occupants of the rental dwelling.
   D.   Identification Of Rental Dwelling And Designation Of Owner's Agent:
      1.   The owner(s) of a rental dwelling must notify the city building
inspector of the existence of said rental dwelling seven (7) or more days prior
to its occupancy, or within seven (7) days from obtaining ownership, on a form
approved by the building inspector including the name(s) of the owner(s) and
manager(s) and agent(s) and the address and telephone number of each. Owner(s)
must notify the city of any changes in ownership, management or agency within
seven (7) days of the change.
      2.   The owner(s) of a rental dwelling must notify the city building
inspector within seven (7) days of a new tenant taking possession of a rental
dwelling if said possession is within three (3) to five (5) years from the last
inspection.
      3.   Every owner of any rental dwelling who does not reside in Logan
County or a county adjoining Logan County shall appoint and designate an
individual to act as an agent in his behalf. Such written notice shall contain
the signature of the agent accepting appointment and designation as agent of
the owner.
      4.   Any individual who is appointed and designated as agent of the owner
shall reside within Logan County, Illinois, or any other Illinois county which
adjoins Logan County, Illinois. An owner of a rental dwelling may act as his
own agent, provided he meets the residency requirements set forth herein.
   E.   Occupants To Provide Access For Inspections And Compliance With Code:
      1.   Each and every occupant of a rental dwelling shall give the owner
thereof, his agent or employee or agents of the building inspector, access to
the rental dwelling, or unit thereof under their control, to conduct
inspections authorized by this section.
      2.   Each and every occupant of a rental dwelling shall give the owner
thereof, or his agent or his employees, access to any part of such rental
dwelling at all reasonable times for the purpose of making such repairs or
alterations as are necessary to effect compliance with the provisions of this
section or with any standard regulation set forth in this code.
   F.   Notice Of Violations:
      1.   If violations are detected by the building inspector, the building
inspector shall notify an owner in writing by delivering a list of the
violations to an owner. The owner shall have thirty (30) days to correct such
violations. Alternatively, within seven (7) days of the notice, the owner may
request additional time to correct the conditions if such request includes a
plan and timetable acceptable to the building inspector. The building inspector
shall reinspect after the thirty (30) days or any agreed upon time has expired,
or sooner upon request of the owner.
      2.   If a rental dwelling is vacant at the time of an inspection, the
rental dwelling may not be occupied without the permission of the building
inspector. If no violations are found, said permission shall be granted
promptly.
   G.   Fees, Fines And Warning Signs:
      1.   There shall be no cost, fee or charge assessed by the city for
inspection of a rental dwelling pursuant to this section whereby no violations
are found. If violation(s) are found, the owner shall be subject to a
reinspection fee of fifty dollars ($50.00). However, should such violations not
be corrected by the time of the first reinspection, the owner shall be subject
to a fee of two hundred dollars ($200.00) for the second reinspection and each
subsequent reinspection until such violations are corrected.
      2.   Any reinspection fees remaining unpaid after two (2) weeks shall be
a debt due and owing the city and, as such, may be collected in accordance with
applicable law.
      3.   Any person violating any of the provisions of this chapter shall be
subject to penalty under the provisions of section
1-4-1 of this code for each offense.
      4.   Any owner failing to correct any conditions found to be in violation
under this chapter within the allotted time shall be subject to penalty under
the provisions of section
1-4-1 of this code. Each violation is a separate offense subject to penalty.
      5.   If a rental dwelling reveals any violations presenting an imminent
threat to human life, health and/or safety of actual or potential occupants,
the building inspector shall install a warning sign or signs on the rental
dwelling and/or on the property on which it is situated, one of which must be
viewable from the street. Said warning sign(s) shall be in a form approved by
the building inspector and at a minimum shall state that the rental dwelling is
uninhabitable by order of the building inspector. Such sign(s) shall not block
access to the property. The building inspector may remove debris or weeds,
install posts, or take other reasonable action to cause such sign(s) to be
viewable from the street.
      6.   Removal, obstruction or otherwise tampering with a warning sign by
anyone other than the building inspector or his agent shall be a violation of
this section.
      7.   Any acts of the city under this section shall not prevent the city
from exercising its rights under chapter 5, "Dangerous Buildings", of this
title. (Ord., 11-9-2010)
TITLE 5
FIRE REGULATIONS
(Rep. per correspondence dated 3-2-2001)
TITLE 6
POLICE REGULATIONS
CHAPTER 1
POLICE DEPARTMENT
SECTION:
6-1-1: Creation Of Department
6-1-2: Office Of Chief Created
6-1-3: Duties Of Chief
6-1-4: Duties Of Members
6-1-5: Conduct Of Members
6-1-6: Probation Period; Rules And Regulations
6-1-7: Special Police
6-1-8: Custody Of Lost, Stolen Property
6-1-9: Intoxicating Beverages, Limitation On Use
6-1-1: CREATION OF DEPARTMENT:
There is hereby created a police department, an executive department of the
city. The police department shall consist of the chief of police and such other
members as may be provided from time to time by the city council. (1967 Code §
8.001)
All police officers, other than those officers who shall be employed on a full
time basis, shall be qualified to enter and successfully complete any training
mandated by the Illinois law enforcement training and standards board.
A part time police officer shall have all the responsibilities of a full time
police officer. Part time officers shall not work more than one thousand five
hundred sixty (1,560) hours in a twelve (12) month period beginning on January
1 of any calendar year. Part time officers shall not be assigned to supervise
or direct full time police officers and shall be trained in accordance with the
Illinois police training act 1  and the rules and requirements of the ILETSB.
Any person employed as a part time officer shall meet the following standards:
   A.   Be at least twenty one (21) years of age.
   B.   Possess a high school diploma or GED certificate.
   C.   Be of good moral character, of sound health, and physically and
mentally able to perform assigned duties.
   D.   Possess a valid Illinois driver's license.
   E.   Have no prior felony convictions.
   F.   Pass a complete medical examination conducted by a licensed physician.
   G.   Any individual with prior military service must have been honorably
discharged.
Part time officers shall serve under the jurisdiction of the chief of police in
all disciplinary matters. Part time officers may be removed from employment at
any time by the chief of police. Part time officers shall comply with all rules
and regulations of the police department as issued by the chief of police, upon
approval by the mayor and city council.
The aforesaid hiring standard, particularly with respect to part time police
officers employed by the city of Mt. Pulaski, Logan County, Illinois, shall be
submitted to the Illinois law enforcement training and standards board, as
required by statute. (Ord., 1-22-2013)
 
Notes
1 1. 50 ILCS 705/1 et seq.
6-1-2: OFFICE OF CHIEF CREATED:
There is hereby created the office of the chief of police. The chief of police
shall be appointed by the mayor, by and with the advice and consent of the city
council, and he shall be ex officio city marshal and superintendent of police.
The chief of police shall serve at the pleasure of the mayor and city council
and be subject to removal at any time by the mayor, with the concurrence of a
majority vote of the city council. If not so removed, he shall hold office
until the expiration of the term of the mayor in office at the time of his
appointment as chief of police, and thereafter, until his successor is
appointed and qualified. (Ord., 10-25-1977)
6-1-3: DUTIES OF CHIEF:
   A.   The chief of police shall keep such records and make such reports
concerning the activities of his department as may be required by statute or
city council. The chief shall be responsible for the performance of the police
department in all of its functions, and all persons who are members of the
department shall serve subject to the orders of the chief of police. The chief
of police shall have sole responsibility and authority to hire and discharge
any employee of the police department. Upon discharging an officer, the chief
of police shall immediately inform the mayor and forward a written detailed
report within two (2) business days to the mayor and city council describing
such actions.
   B.   If the office of chief of police is vacant, or he/she is unable to
perform his/her duties, the city council police committee has the authority to
perform the administrative duties assigned to the chief until such vacancy is
filled either permanently or by temporary appointment, or when the chief of
police is able to continue his/her duties. (Ord., 7-14-2015)
6-1-4: DUTIES OF MEMBERS:
It shall be the duty of the members of the police department to see to the
enforcement of all of the ordinances of the city and all statutes applicable
therein; and to preserve order and prevent infractions of the law, and arrest
violators thereof. (1967 Code § 8.004)
6-1-5: CONDUCT OF MEMBERS:
It shall be the duty of every member of the police department to conduct
himself in a proper and law abiding manner at all times, and to avoid the use
of unnecessary force. Each member of the department shall obey the orders and
directions of his superior. (1967 Code § 8.007)
6-1-6: PROBATION PERIOD; RULES AND REGULATIONS:
All newly employed members of the police department shall serve a continuous
one year probation period, commencing with the date of employment, before
entering into regular contractual service with the city. The chief of police
may make or prescribe such rules and regulations for the hours of duty,
vacations, uniforms and conduct of the members of the police department as he
shall deem advisable, and such rules, when approved by the mayor and council,
shall be binding on such members. (Ord., 10-25-1977)
6-1-7: SPECIAL POLICE:
Any person of good character having duties which require it, may be appointed a
special police officer by the chief of police; provided, that except upon
authorization by the city council, no such special police officer shall be
entitled to any compensation from the city, nor shall such special police
officer be considered an employee of the city by reason of such appointment.
Special police officers shall obey all rules of the police department
applicable thereto, and may be deprived of their appointment by the chief at
any time. (1967 Code § 8.010)
6-1-8: CUSTODY OF LOST, STOLEN PROPERTY:
The chief of police shall be the custodian of all lost and abandoned or stolen
property in the city. Property is to be retained at the police department,
locked in a safe place to prevent theft and pilferage, and a record of such
property and disposition of same filed with the city clerk.
Abandoned or stolen property in possession of the chief of police in excess of
ninety (90) days, not properly identified or claimed, may be disposed of by
public sale and funds derived from such sale turned over to the city clerk.
(1967 Code § 8.011; amd. 1977 Code)
6-1-9: INTOXICATING BEVERAGES, LIMITATION ON USE:
No regular or probationary member of the police department shall partake of any
form of intoxicating beverage during the four (4) hours immediately preceding
the commencement of time of active duty. (Ord., 10-25-1977)
CHAPTER 2
GENERAL OFFENSES
SECTION:
6-2-1: Advertisements
6-2-2: Assemblages
6-2-3: Bathing
6-2-4: Combustible Refuse; Depositing Refuse On Public Ways
6-2-5: Possession, Consumption Of Alcoholic Beverages On Public Ways
6-2-6: Conduct In Liquor Establishments
6-2-7: Discharge Of Firearms
6-2-8: Injurious Materials On Thoroughfares
6-2-9: Injury To Public Property
6-2-10: Throwing Missiles
6-2-11: Noises
6-2-12: Posting Bills
6-2-13: Profanity
6-2-14: Articles On Window Ledges
6-2-15: Penalty
6-2-1: ADVERTISEMENTS:
   A.   It shall be unlawful to advertise any unlawful business or article in
the city, and it shall be unlawful to injure or deface any lawful advertisement
or notice. (1967 Code § 28.012)
   B.   It shall be unlawful for any person, by himself or his agents or
servants, to distribute, cast, throw or place, or cause to be distributed,
cast, thrown or placed, in, upon or along any of the streets, alleys or other
public places of the city, or upon the porches or yards of private residences
therein, or within any dwelling or building in the city any samples of
merchandise or medicinal preparations for the purpose or with the intent of
advertising or making known in a general or promiscuous manner any business,
occupation, proposition, medical treatment, medicine or other article
whatsoever. (1967 Code § 28.019)
6-2-2: ASSEMBLAGES:
   A.   It shall be unlawful for any person to disturb any lawful assemblage or
gathering in the city. (1967 Code § 28.008)
   B.   It shall be unlawful to collect, gather or be a member of any
disorderly crowd, or any crowd gathered together for any unlawful purpose.
(1967 Code § 28.013)
   C.   It shall be unlawful for any person to loiter or congregate upon the
streets, sidewalks or alleys of the city in the vicinity of any place of
worship, school, theater, hotel, store, factory or other public place to the
annoyance or disturbance of any person or persons. Any number of persons who
shall congregate upon such public places and shall refuse to disperse when
requested to do so by any member of the police force or by any person annoyed
thereby shall be subject to penalty as provided in section
6-2-15 of this chapter. (Ord., 9-14-2004; amd. 2010 Code)
6-2-3: BATHING:
It shall be unlawful for any person to bathe at any public place or in any
place open to the public view unless such person is adequately garbed in a
bathing suit. (1967 Code § 28.016)
6-2-4: COMBUSTIBLE REFUSE; DEPOSITING REFUSE ON PUBLIC WAYS 1 :
It shall be unlawful to permit or store any combustible refuse in such a way as
to create a fire hazard, or to store or throw refuse of any kind on any alley,
street or other public place in the city. (1967 Code § 28.010)
 
Notes
1 1. See also section
  7-3-2 of this code.
6-2-5: POSSESSION, CONSUMPTION OF ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGES ON PUBLIC WAYS:
   A.   It shall be unlawful for any person to possess an alcoholic beverage,
with the seal broken on the container thereof, or consume an alcoholic beverage
on any public street, sidewalk, or alley or on any public grounds within the
corporate limits of the city.
   B.   Notwithstanding the foregoing, if a request is made to the city
council, and the city council approves the specific times, date and location
boundaries for a specific onetime event lasting no longer than two (2)
consecutive days, it shall be lawful for a person to possess an alcoholic
beverage, with the seal broken on the container thereof, or consume an
alcoholic beverage, on the designated public street, sidewalk, or alley or
public grounds within the corporate limits of the city during the authorized
times and dates, subject to issuance of a permit or license by the liquor
commissioner. (Ord., 6-9-2015)
6-2-6: CONDUCT IN LIQUOR ESTABLISHMENTS:
No licensee or other person in charge of a premises licensed for the sale of
alcoholic liquor shall permit the use or utterance of obscene or profane
language at said premises or any act creating a disturbance without protest;
and if the protest goes unheeded, such person in charge shall forthwith notify
the police department and request assistance, if necessary, to eject the
offender. Any person who shall so use obscene or profane language or who shall
create any disturbance, as aforesaid, in or on said premises shall be deemed
guilty of violating this section. (1977 Code)
6-2-7: DISCHARGE OF FIREARMS:
It shall be unlawful to discharge any firearms or air gun in the city;
provided, that this section shall not be construed to prohibit any officer of
the law from discharging a firearm in the performance of his duty, nor any
citizen from discharging a firearm when lawfully defending his person or
property. (1967 Code § 28.015)
6-2-8: INJURIOUS MATERIALS ON THOROUGHFARES:
It shall be unlawful to throw or deposit any glass, nails, tacks or other
articles on any street, alley, sidewalk or other public place in the city.
(1967 Code § 28.026)
6-2-9: INJURY TO PUBLIC PROPERTY:
It shall be unlawful for anyone to injure, deface or interfere with any
property belonging to the city without proper authority from the city council.
(1967 Code § 10.703; amd. 1977 Code; 2010 Code)
6-2-10: THROWING MISSILES:
It shall be unlawful to cast, throw or propel any missile on any street, alley
or public place. (1967 Code § 28.011; amd. 2010 Code)
6-2-11: NOISES 1 :
It shall be unlawful to do any of the following acts:
   A.   To make or cause to be made any noise or sounds of such volume or of
such a nature as to cause annoyance to residents of the city.
   B.   To disturb the peace by the making of any unnecessary noise.
   C.   To operate any pneumatic hammer, grinding or crushing machinery, mixing
or loading machine, or any other machinery, equipment or device in the city
which makes or causes a noise in violation of any of the provisions of this
section. (1967 Code § 28.028)
   D.   To permit live entertainment and/or live music in any business
establishment within the corporate limits of the city after twelve o'clock (12:
00) midnight, except where special permission is given by the mayor, subject to
approval by the city council 2 . (Ord., 6-11-1985)
 
Notes
1 1. See title 3, chapter 6 of this code for sound amplifier regulations.
2 1. See also section
  3-2A-4 of this code.
6-2-12: POSTING BILLS:
It shall be unlawful to post any bills or advertisements on any public property
without the authority of the city council, and it shall be unlawful to post any
bill or advertisement on any property without the written consent of the owner
thereof. (1967 Code § 28.017)
6-2-13: PROFANITY:
It shall be unlawful to use any profanity in any street, alley or other public
place in the city. (1967 Code § 28.003)
6-2-14: ARTICLES ON WINDOW LEDGES:
It shall be unlawful to place any movable articles on any window ledge or other
place abutting a public street, alley or other place at a height above four
feet (4') from the ground in such a manner that the same can be or is in danger
of falling onto such street, alley, sidewalk or other public place. (1967 Code
§ 28.022)
6-2-15: PENALTY:
Unless otherwise provided, any person violating any provision of this chapter
shall be subject to penalty under the provisions of section
1-4-1 of this code for each offense, and a separate offense shall be deemed
committed on each day during or on which violation occurs or continues. (Ord.,
7-9-1991; amd. 2010 Code)
CHAPTER 3
ANIMAL CONTROL
SECTION:
6-3-1: Cruelty
6-3-2: Prohibited Animals
6-3-3: Noises
6-3-4: Diseased Animals
6-3-5: Housing
6-3-6: Penalty
6-3-1: CRUELTY:
No person shall cruelly treat any animal in the city in any way. Any person who
inhumanely beats, overloads, underfeeds or abandons any animal shall be deemed
guilty of a violation of this section. (1967 Code § 26.101)
Each owner shall provide for each animal a sufficient quantity of food and
water, and adequate protection from the weather. (Ord., 9-9-2008)
6-3-2: PROHIBITED ANIMALS:
   A.   It shall be unlawful for any person to own, use, keep or permit to be
at large within the city limits any of the following animals: bees, horses,
cattle, sheep, goats, ponies, mules, pigs, swine, hogs, ducks, geese, minks,
skunks, foxes, chinchillas or any other livestock or poultry or any wild or
vicious animal dangerous to human beings. Rabbits shall be permitted up to five
(5) per household and shall not be raised for human consumption. Chickens shall
be permitted up to five (5) per household. Roosters are prohibited. All
chickens shall be kept within a pen, coop, building or other enclosure
sufficient in size and strength to confine such animals to the owner's property
and protect them from weather and cold. These enclosures must have a minimum of
four (4) square feet per chicken with a one hundred (100) square foot maximum
size, shall not be erected or maintained within fifteen feet (15') of any
occupied residence other than that of the owner and be kept clean. (Ord., 7-14-
2015)
Section
6-3-6 of this chapter and section
7-1-2 of this code shall apply to foul odor and housing conditions regarding
rabbits. (Ord., 5-25-2010)
   B.   It shall be unlawful to permit any dangerous or vicious animal of any
kind to run at large in the city. Exhibitions or parades of animals which are
ferae naturae in the eyes of the law may be conducted only upon securing a
permit from the city council.
   C.   The members of the police department or any other persons in the city
are authorized to kill any dangerous animal when it is necessary for the
protection of any person or property. (Ord., 5-11-2004)
6-3-3: NOISES:
No person shall, in the city, keep or harbor any dog, cat, or other animal
which, by barking, howling, bawling, or by other noises, shall disturb the
peace and quiet of any family, individual or neighborhood; and every person
violating this section shall forfeit and pay to the city, within seventy two
(72) hours of the date of the ticket charging such alleged offense, not less
than twenty five dollars ($25.00) for the first offense and not less than fifty
dollars ($50.00) for each subsequent offense alleged to have occurred within a
twelve (12) month period. Payment of the fine above shall be made at the police
station or at the city hall and a receipt issued for the money so received, and
said money shall be promptly turned over to the city treasurer. If not paid as
above, a written complaint for a violation of this section shall be obtained
and issued through the city attorney and served by certified mail on the person
or persons charged with the offense along with a notice to appear to answer
said charge. Any person found guilty by a court of law or jury of violating the
provisions of this section shall be subject to the penalty provisions of
section
6-3-6 of this chapter. (Ord., 9-10-1996; amd. 2010 Code)
6-3-4: DISEASED ANIMALS:
No domestic animal afflicted with a contagious disease or an infectious disease
shall be allowed to run at large or be exposed in any public place whereby the
health of man or beast may be affected, nor shall such diseased animal be
shipped or removed from the premises of the owner thereof except under the
supervision of the county health officer. (1967 Code § 26.106; amd. 1977 Code;
2010 Code)
It is hereby made the duty of the chief of police to secure such disposition of
any diseased animal and such treatment of affected premises as to prevent the
communication or spread of contagion or infection, except in cases where the
state veterinarian is empowered to act. (1967 Code § 26.106; amd. 1977 Code)
6-3-5: HOUSING:
No person shall allow any place where any animal is or may be kept to become
unclean or unwholesome. (1967 Code § 26.107; amd. 1977 Code; 2010 Code)
6-3-6: PENALTY:
Any person violating any provision of this chapter shall be subject to penalty
under the provisions of section
1-4-1 of this code for each offense, and a separate offense shall be deemed
committed on each day during or on which a violation occurs or continues. (1977
Code)
CHAPTER 4
DOGS
SECTION:
6-4-1: Running At Large/Intimidation
6-4-2: Registration Required
6-4-3: Registration Fee
6-4-4: Rabies Inoculation
6-4-5: Restraint
6-4-6: Impoundment And Disposition
6-4-7: Dog Bite
6-4-8: Penalties
6-4-1: RUNNING AT LARGE/INTIMIDATION:
   A.   It shall be unlawful to permit any dog to run at large within the city.
Any dog found upon any public street, sidewalk, alley, parkway, or any
unenclosed place without being held securely on a leash, or in an enclosed
vehicle, shall be deemed to be running at large.
   B.   It shall be unlawful to permit any dog to run at large on the private
property of anyone but the owner or lessee thereof without the permission of an
owner or lessee of said property.
   C.   It shall be unlawful to allow any dog to chase, attack, bite, interfere
with or physically intimidate any person or other animal while on or off of the
premises of the owner.
   D.   Any such dog in violation of this section may be impounded and dealt
with as provided in section
6-4-6 of this chapter and, in such case, shall be subject to the penalty
provisions of section
6-4-8 of this chapter. (Ord., 6-26-2012)
6-4-2: REGISTRATION REQUIRED:
It shall be the duty of every person owning, keeping or harboring any dog in
the city to register the same with the rabies and animal control officer of
Logan County. (1967 Code § 26.201)
6-4-3: REGISTRATION FEE:
The fee for registration shall be as stipulated by Logan County ordinance.
(1967 Code § 26.202)
6-4-4: RABIES INOCULATION:
It shall be the duty of the owner or person in custody of any dog kept in the
city to have the dog inoculated against rabies at least once each year. The dog
owner or custodian shall obtain and keep as a matter of record and shall
exhibit or show to any officer of the city a certificate by a veterinarian
showing compliance with this section. (1967 Code § 26.203)
6-4-5: RESTRAINT:
It shall be unlawful to permit any dog to go upon any public street, alley or
sidewalk or other public place unless such dog is on a chain or leash. (1967
Code § 26.204; amd. 2010 Code)
6-4-6: IMPOUNDMENT AND DISPOSITION:
Animals found running at large shall be taken into custody and shall be
impounded at a pound location as determined and specified by county ordinance.
Disposal of animals impounded will be in accordance with county ordinance.
(1967 Code § 26.206; amd. 2010 Code)
6-4-7: DOG BITE:
Whenever any dog bites a person, the owner of said dog shall immediately notify
the chief of police who shall order the dog to be held on the owner's premises
or shall have it impounded for a period of ten (10) days. The dog shall be
examined immediately after it has bitten anyone and again at the end of the ten
(10) day period.
If, at the end of this ten (10) day period, a veterinarian is convinced that
the dog is free from rabies, he shall order the dog released from quarantine or
the pound as the case may be. (Ord., 5-28-1974)
6-4-8: PENALTIES:
Any person violating subsection
6-4-1C of this chapter shall be subject to the penalty provisions of
subsections B, C and D of this section. Any person violating any other section
of this chapter shall be subject to the penalty provisions of subsections A, C
and D of this section.
   A.   The sum of thirty five dollars ($35.00) for the first violation and
fifty dollars ($50.00) for the second and subsequent violations of the violator
in any one year period.
   B.   The sum of two hundred dollars ($200.00) for the first violation, three
hundred fifty dollars ($350.00) for the second violation, and five hundred
dollars ($500.00) for the third and subsequent violations of the violator in
any two (2) year period.
   C.   Said fines shall be paid to the city within seventy two (72) hours of
the date of the ticket charging such alleged offense at the police station or
at the city hall. A receipt shall be issued for all monies so received, and
said monies shall be promptly turned over to the city treasurer.
   D.   If the above fine is not paid within seventy two (72) hours of the date
of the ticket charging such offense, a written complaint for a violation of
this chapter shall be obtained and issued through the city attorney and served
by certified mail, or by personal or abode service by the sheriff, on the
person or persons charged with the offense along with a notice to appear to
answer said charge. Any person found guilty in a court of law of violating any
provision of this chapter shall be subject to penalty under the provisions of
section
1-4-1 of this code for each offense. (Ord., 6-26-2012)
CHAPTER 5
MINORS
SECTION:
6-5-1: Curfew
6-5-1: CURFEW:
   A.   Definitions: As used in this section, the following words and terms
shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection:
    CURFEW HOURS:
      1.   Between one minute after twelve o'clock (12:01) A.M. and six o'clock
(6:00) A.M. on Saturday;
      2.   Between one minute after twelve o'clock (12:01) A.M. and six o'clock
(6:00) A.M. on Sunday; and
      3.   Between eleven o'clock (11:00) P.M. on Sunday to Thursday,
inclusive, and six o'clock (6:00) A.M. on the following day.
   EMERGENCY: An unforeseen combination of circumstances or the resulting state
that calls for immediate action. The term includes, but is not limited to, a
fire, a natural disaster, an automobile accident, or any situation requiring
immediate action to prevent serious bodily injury or loss of life.
   ESTABLISHMENT: Any privately owned place of business operated for a profit
to which the public is invited including, but not limited to, any place of
amusement or entertainment.
   GUARDIAN:
      1.   A person who, under court order, is the guardian of the person of a
minor; or
      2.   A public or private agency with whom a minor has been placed by a
court.
   MINOR: Any person under seventeen (17) years of age.
   PARENT: A person who is:
      1.   A natural parent, adoptive parent or  stepparent of another person;
or
      2.   At least eighteen (18) years of age and authorized by a parent or
guardian to have the care and custody of a minor.
   PUBLIC PLACE: Any place to which the public or a substantial group of the
public has access and includes, but is not limited to, streets, highways, and
the common areas of schools, hospitals, apartment houses, office buildings,
transport facilities, and shops.
   REMAIN: To:
      1.   Linger or stay; or
      2.   Fail to leave premises when requested to do so by a police officer
or the owner, operator, or other person in control of the premises.
   SERIOUS BODILY INJURY: Bodily injury that creates a substantial risk of
death or that causes death, serious permanent disfigurement, or protracted loss
or impairment of the function of any bodily member or organ.
   B.   Offenses:
      1.   A minor commits an offense if he or she remains in any public place
or on the premises of any establishment during curfew hours.
      2.   A parent or guardian of a minor or other person in custody or
control of a minor commits an offense if he or she knowingly permits the minor
to remain in any public place or on the premises of any establishment during
curfew hours.
   C.   Defenses: It is a defense to prosecution under subsection B of this
section that the minor was:
      1.   Accompanied by the minor's parent or guardian or other person in
custody or control of the minor;
      2.   On an errand at the direction of the minor's parent or guardian,
without any detour or stop;
      3.   In a motor vehicle involved in interstate travel;
      4.   Engaged in an employment activity or going to or returning home from
an employment activity, without any detour or stop;
      5.   Involved in an emergency;
      6.   On the sidewalk abutting the minor's residence or abutting the
residence of a next door neighbor if the neighbor did not complain to the
police department about the minor's presence;
      7.   Attending an official school, religious, or other recreational
activity supervised by adults and sponsored by a government or governmental
agency, a civic organization, or another similar entity that takes
responsibility for the minor, or going to or returning home from, without any
detour or stop, an official school, religious, or other recreational activity
supervised by adults and sponsored by a government or governmental agency, a
civic organization, or another similar entity that takes responsibility for the
minor;
      8.   Exercising first amendment rights protected by the United States
constitution, such as the free exercise of religion, freedom of speech, and the
right of assembly; or
      9.   Married or had been married or is an emancipated minor under the
emancipation of minors act 1 .
   D.   Enforcement: Before taking any enforcement action under this section, a
law enforcement officer shall ask the apparent offender's age and reason for
being in the public place. The officer shall not issue a citation or make an
arrest under this section unless the officer reasonably believes that an
offense has occurred and that, based on any response and other circumstances,
no defense in subsection C of this section is present.
   E.   Violation; Penalties: A person convicted of a violation of any
provision of this section shall be guilty of a petty offense and shall be fined
not less than ten dollars ($10.00) nor more than five hundred dollars
($500.00); except, that neither a person who has been made a ward of the court
under the juvenile court act of 1987 2 , nor that person's legal guardian,
shall be subject to any fine. In addition to or instead of the fine imposed by
this section, the court may order a parent, legal guardian, or other person
convicted of a violation of subsection B of this section to perform community
service as determined by the court; except, that the legal guardian of a person
who has been made a ward of the court under the juvenile court act of 1987 may
not be ordered to perform community service. The dates and times established
for the performance of community service by the parent, legal guardian, or
other person convicted of a violation of subsection B of this section shall not
conflict with the dates and times that the person is employed in his or her
regular occupation. (2010 Code)
 
Notes
1 1. 750 ILCS 30/1 et seq.
2 2. 705 ILCS 405/1-1 et seq.
CHAPTER 6
ABANDONED, WRECKED, NUISANCE VEHICLES
ARTICLE A.  ABANDONED, WRECKED VEHICLES
SECTION:
6-6A-1: Definitions
6-6A-2: Abandonment Prohibited
6-6A-3: Notify Police Department
6-6A-4: Removal
6-6A-5: Records Kept
6-6A-6: Owner Unknown
6-6A-7: Notify State Police
6-6A-8: Reclamation Of Vehicle
6-6A-9: Notice Of Sale
6-6A-10: Sale Without Notice; Disposition
6-6A-11: Report Maintained
6-6A-12: Proceeds Of Sale
6-6A-13: Nonliability Of Police And Towing Service
6-6A-14: Exemptions From Provisions
6-6A-1: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this chapter, the following words shall have the meanings
ascribed to them as follows:
ABANDONED VEHICLE: Any motor vehicle or other vehicle in a state of disrepair
rendering the vehicle incapable of being driven in its condition; or any motor
vehicle or other vehicle that has not been used for seven (7) consecutive days
or more and is apparently deserted.
ANTIQUE VEHICLE: Any motor vehicle or other vehicle twenty five (25) years of
age or older.
HIGHWAY: Any street, alley or public way within the city. (1977 Code; amd.
Ord., 10-14-1997)
6-6A-2: ABANDONMENT PROHIBITED:
The abandonment of a motor vehicle or other vehicle or any part thereof on any
highway in the city is unlawful and subject to penalties as set forth in this
code. The abandonment of a motor vehicle or other vehicle or any part thereof
on private or public property, other than a highway, in view of the general
public, anywhere in the city is unlawful except on property of the owner or
bailee of such abandoned vehicle. A motor vehicle or other vehicle or any part
thereof so abandoned on private property may be authorized for removal by or
upon the order of the chief of police, after a waiting period of seven (7) days
or more has expired. (1977 Code)
6-6A-3: NOTIFY POLICE DEPARTMENT:
When an abandoned, lost, stolen or unclaimed motor vehicle or other vehicle
comes into the temporary possession or custody of a person in the city, not the
owner of the vehicle, such person shall immediately notify the city police
department when the vehicle is within the corporate limits of the city. Upon
receipt of such notification, the chief of police shall authorize a towing
service to remove and take possession of the abandoned, lost, stolen or
unclaimed motor vehicle or other vehicle. The towing service will safely keep
the towed vehicle and its contents and maintain a record of the tow until the
vehicle is claimed by the owner or any other person legally entitled to
possession thereof, or until it is disposed of as provided in this article.
(1977 Code; amd. 2010 Code)
6-6A-4: REMOVAL:
   A.   When a motor vehicle or other vehicle is abandoned on a highway in the
city ten (10) hours or more, its removal by a towing service may be authorized
by order of the chief of police.
   B.   When an abandoned, unattended, wrecked, burned or partially dismantled
motor vehicle or other vehicle is creating a traffic hazard because of its
position in relation to the highway or its physical appearance is causing the
impeding of traffic, its immediate removal from the highway by a towing service
may be authorized by order of the chief of the police department.
   C.   When a vehicle removed from either public or private property is
authorized by order of the chief of police, the owner of the vehicle will be
responsible for all towing costs. (1977 Code)
6-6A-5: RECORDS KEPT:
When a motor vehicle or other vehicle is authorized to be towed, the police
department shall keep and maintain a record of the vehicle towed, listing the
color, year of manufacture, manufacturer's trade name, manufacturer's series
name, body style, vehicle identification number and license plate year and
number displayed on the vehicle. The record shall also include the date and
hour of tow, location towed from, location towed to, reason for towing and the
name of the officer authorizing the tow. (1977 Code)
6-6A-6: OWNER UNKNOWN:
When the city police department does not know the identity of the registered
owner or other legally entitled person, they will cause the motor vehicle
registration records of the state of Illinois to be searched by a directed
communication to the secretary of state for the purpose of obtaining the
required ownership information.
The police department will cause the stolen motor vehicle files of the Illinois
state police to be searched by a directed communication to the Illinois state
police for stolen or wanted information on the vehicle. When the Illinois state
police files are searched with negative results, the information contained in
the national crime information center (NCIC) files will be searched by the
Illinois state police. The information determined from these record searches
will be used by the police department in sending a notification by certified
mail to the owner or legally entitled person advising where the vehicle is
held, requesting a disposition be made and setting forth public sale
information. (1977 Code)
6-6A-7: NOTIFY STATE POLICE:
When the registered owner or other person legally entitled to the possession of
a motor vehicle or other vehicle cannot be identified from the registration
files of this state or from the registration files of a foreign state, if
applicable, the police department shall notify the Illinois state police for
the purpose of identifying the vehicle's owner or other person legally entitled
to the possession of the vehicle. The information obtained by the Illinois
state police will be immediately forwarded to the city police department for
notification of the owner. (1977 Code; amd. 2010 Code)
6-6A-8: RECLAMATION OF VEHICLE:
Anytime before a motor vehicle or other vehicle is sold at public sale or
disposed of as provided herein, the owner or other person legally entitled to
its possession may reclaim the vehicle by presenting to the police department
proof of ownership or proof of the right to possession of the vehicle. No
vehicle shall be released to the owner or other person under this section until
all towing and storage charges have been paid. (1977 Code)
6-6A-9: NOTICE OF SALE:
Whenever an abandoned, lost, stolen or unclaimed motor vehicle or other
vehicle, seven (7) years of age or newer, remains unclaimed by the registered
owner or other person legally entitled to its possession for a period of thirty
(30) days after notice has been given as provided herein, the police department
having possession of the vehicle shall cause it to be sold at public sale to
the highest bidder. Notice of the time and place of the sale shall be posted in
a conspicuous place for at least ten (10) days prior to the sale on the
premises where the vehicle has been impounded. At least ten (10) days prior to
the sale, the police department shall cause a notice of the time and place of
the sale to be sent by certified mail to the registered owner or other person
known by the police department or towing service to be legally entitled to the
possession of the vehicle. Such notice shall contain a complete description of
the vehicle to be sold and what steps must be taken by any legally entitled
person to reclaim the vehicle.
In those instances where the certified notification specified herein has been
returned by the postal authorities to the police department due to the
addressee having moved, or being unknown at the address obtained from the
registration records of this state, the sending of a second certified notice
will not be required. (1977 Code)
6-6A-10: SALE WITHOUT NOTICE; DISPOSITION:
When the identity of the registered owner or other person legally entitled to
the possession of an abandoned, lost or unclaimed vehicle of seven (7) years of
age or newer cannot be determined by any means provided in this article, the
vehicle may be sold as provided herein or disposed of in the manner authorized
by this article without notice to the registered owner or other person legally
entitled to the possession of the vehicle.
When an abandoned vehicle of more than seven (7) years of age is impounded as
specified by this article, it will be kept in custody for a minimum of ten (10)
days for the purpose of determining ownership, the contacting of the registered
owner by the U.S. mail, public service or in person for a determination of
disposition, and an examination of the Illinois state police stolen motor
vehicle files for theft and wanted information. At the expiration of the ten
(10) day period, without the benefit of disposition being received from the
registered owner, the chief of police will authorize the disposal of the
vehicle as junk only. (1977 Code)
6-6A-11: REPORT MAINTAINED:
When a motor vehicle or other vehicle in the custody of the police department
is reclaimed by the registered owner or other legally entitled person, or when
the vehicle is sold at public sale or otherwise disposed of as provided in this
article, a report of the transaction will be maintained by the police
department for a period of one year from the date of the sale or disposal.
(1977 Code)
6-6A-12: PROCEEDS OF SALE:
When a vehicle located within the corporate limits of the city is authorized to
be towed away by the chief of police and disposed of as set forth in this
article, the proceeds of the public sale or disposition after the deduction of
towing, storage and processing charges shall be deposited in the municipal
treasury. (1977 Code)
6-6A-13: NONLIABILITY OF POLICE AND TOWING SERVICE:
Any police officer or towing service owner, operator or employee shall not be
held to answer or be liable for damages brought by the registered owner, former
registered owner or his legal representatives, or any other person legally
entitled to the possession of a motor vehicle or other vehicle when the vehicle
was processed and sold or disposed of as provided by this article. (1977 Code)
6-6A-14: EXEMPTIONS FROM PROVISIONS:
A motor vehicle or other vehicle classified as an antique vehicle is excluded
from this article. (1977 Code)
ARTICLE B.  NUISANCE VEHICLES
SECTION:
6-6B-1: Definitions
6-6B-2: Nuisance Declared
6-6B-3: Removal; Notice
6-6B-4: Abatement
6-6B-5: Lien; Foreclosure
6-6B-6: Penalty
6-6B-1: DEFINITIONS:
INOPERABLE MOTOR VEHICLE: Any motor vehicle from which, for a period of at
least seven (7) days, the engine, wheels or other parts have been removed, or
on which the engine, wheels or other parts have been altered, damaged or
otherwise so treated that the vehicle is incapable of being driven under its
own motor power. The term "inoperable motor vehicle" also includes any motor
vehicle that is unlicensed or unregistered or bears expired, suspended, or
revoked registration such to render the operation of the same illegal under the
laws of the state of Illinois or the ordinances of the city of Mt. Pulaski. The
term "inoperable motor vehicle" shall not include a motor vehicle which has
been rendered temporarily incapable of being driven under its own motor power
in order to perform ordinary service or repair work. This article also does not
apply to any motor vehicle that is kept within a building when not in use, to
operable historic vehicles over twenty five (25) years of age, or to a motor
vehicle on the premises of a place of business engaged in the wrecking or
junking of motor vehicles.
TRAILER: Every vehicle without motive power in operation, other than a pole
trailer, designed for carrying persons or property and for being drawn by a
motor vehicle and so constructed that no part of its weight rests upon the
towing vehicle 1 . Trailers must display current and legal registration. Wheels
and other parts cannot be altered, disassembled, damaged or otherwise so
treated as to render it inoperable.
TRAVEL TRAILER: A trailer, not used commercially, designed to provide living
quarters for recreational, camping or travel use, and of a size or weight not
requiring an overdimension permit when towed on a highway 2 . Travel trailers
must display current and legal registration. Wheels and other parts cannot be
altered, disassembled, damaged or otherwise so treated as to render it
inoperable. (Ord., 4-9-2013)
 
Notes
1 1. 625 ILCS 5/1-209.
2 2. 625 ILCS 5/1-210.01.
6-6B-2: NUISANCE DECLARED:
An inoperable motor vehicle, travel trailer or trailer on public or private
property, and in view of the general public, is hereby declared to be a
nuisance. No person in charge or in control of the premises, whether as an
owner, lessee, tenant, occupant or otherwise, shall allow an "inoperable motor
vehicle", "travel trailer", or "trailer" as defined in section
6-6B-1 of this article, to remain on his property for more than seven (7) days.
A "travel trailer" or "trailer", as defined above, whether on public or private
property, and in view of the general public, lacking current, legal
registration is hereby declared to be a nuisance. At no time shall any vehicle,
travel trailer or trailer of any type, undergo a disassembly of parts, commonly
called stripping, or a major overhaul, including bodywork, outside of an
enclosed structure where a vehicle, travel trailer or trailer would be in
violation of this article. Any person in charge or in control of the premises,
whether as an owner, lessee, tenant, occupant or otherwise, shall be subject to
a fine pursuant to section
1-4-1, "General Penalty", of this code for failure to abate the nuisance(s) as
declared by the city code official. The owner or person in possession or
control of an inoperable motor vehicle, travel trailer or trailer, upon being
served a notice to abate the nuisance vehicle, shall not move the vehicle,
travel trailer or trailer to another location within the city limits where the
vehicle would be in violation of this article. (Ord., 4-9-2013)
6-6B-3: REMOVAL; NOTICE:
It shall be the duty of the chief of police to serve or cause to be served a
notice upon the owner or person in possession or control of an inoperable motor
vehicle, travel trailer or trailer, or parts thereof in violation of the
provisions of this article, and to demand that such vehicle or parts thereof be
disposed of and to abate the nuisance within seven (7) days from the issuance
of the notice. (Ord., 4-9-2013)
6-6B-4: ABATEMENT:
If the person in possession or control of the property cannot be located so as
to serve a notice of violation as provided in section
6-6B-3 of this article the city may proceed to abate the nuisance, keeping an
account of the expense of the abatement, and such expense shall be charged and
