8-9-2: PRIVATE WATER SUPPLY:
No person shall establish or permit to be established or maintain or permit to
be maintained any connection whereby a private, auxiliary or emergency water
supply, other than the regular public water supply of the city, enters the
supply or distribution system of the city, unless such private, auxiliary or
emergency water supply and the method of connection and use of such supply
shall have been approved by the superintendent of water and the Illinois
environmental protection agency. (Ord., 1-26-1988)
8-9-3: SURVEYS AND INVESTIGATIONS:
It shall be the duty of the superintendent of water to cause surveys and
investigations to be made of industrial and other properties served by the
public water supply to determine whether actual or potential hazards to the
public water supply may exist. Such surveys and investigations shall be made a
matter of public record and shall be repeated at least every two (2) years, or
as often as the superintendent of water shall deem necessary. Records of such
surveys shall be maintained and available for review for a period of at least
five (5) years. (Ord., 1-26-1988)
8-9-4: RIGHT OF ENTRY:
The approved cross connection control device inspector shall have the right to
enter at any reasonable time any property served by a connection to the public
water supply or distribution system of the city for the purpose of verifying
the presence or absence of cross connections, and the water superintendent or
his authorized agent shall have the right to enter at any reasonable time any
property served by a connection to the public water supply or distribution
system of the city for the purpose of verifying information submitted by the
customer regarding the required cross connection control inspection. On demand,
the owner, lessees or occupants of any property so served shall furnish to the
superintendent of water any information which he may request regarding the
piping system or systems for water use on such property. The refusal of such
information, when demanded, shall, within the discretion of the superintendent
of water, be deemed evidence of the presence of improper connections as
provided in this chapter. (Ord., 1-26-1988)
8-9-5: NOTICE OF DISCONNECTION OF WATER SERVICE:
The superintendent of water of the city is hereby authorized and directed to
discontinue, after reasonable notice to the occupant thereof, the water service
to any property wherein any connection in violation of the provisions of this
chapter is known to exist, and to take such other precautionary measures as he
may deem necessary to eliminate any danger of contamination of the public water
supply distribution mains. Water service to such property shall not be restored
until such conditions have been eliminated or corrected in compliance with the
provisions of this chapter, and until a reconnection fee of one hundred dollars
($100.00) is paid to the city. Immediate disconnection with verbal notice can
be effected when the superintendent of water is assured that imminent danger of
harmful contamination of the public water supply system exists. Such action
shall be followed by written notification of the cause of disconnection. (Ord.,
1-26-1988; amd. 2010 Code)
8-9-6: COSTS:
The consumer responsible for backsiphoned material or contamination through
backflow, if contamination of the potable water supply system occurs through an
illegal cross connection or an improperly installed, maintained or repaired
device, or a device which has been bypassed, must bear the cost of cleanup of
the potable water supply system. (Ord., 1-26-1988)
8-9-7: ADOPTION OF REGULATIONS:
The city hereby adopts, and makes a part of this chapter, regulations of cross
connection control in accordance with those certain regulations on cross
connection control adopted contemporaneously with this chapter in printed form
and available for inspection in the city clerk's office. (Ord., 1-26-1988)
CHAPTER 10
WATER SERVICE EMERGENCY; WATER RESTRICTIONS
SECTION:
8-10-1: Preamble
8-10-2: Definitions
8-10-3: Water Service Emergency Declared By The Mayor
8-10-4: Stages Of Water Restriction
8-10-5: Fines And Penalties
8-10-1: PREAMBLE:
The city council of Mt. Pulaski, Illinois, finds that the Mt. Pulaski water
department was developed and is maintained to provide water to the citizens of
the city of Mt. Pulaski. Its primary purpose is to supply water to the citizens
of the city of Mt. Pulaski to further their health and welfare. Therefore, when
it appears that the city water supply is at a level such that fulfilling that
purpose is compromised, it is necessary to put water restrictions in place.
If any clause of this chapter is determined to be unenforceable, the remainder
of this chapter shall remain intact and enforceable. If this chapter conflicts
with any other ordinance of the city, this chapter shall take precedence.
(Ord., 7-24-2012)
8-10-2: DEFINITIONS:
For the purposes of this chapter, the following terms, phrases, words and their
derivations shall have the meaning given herein. When not inconsistent with the
context, words used in the present tense include the future, words in the
plural number include the singular number, and words in the singular number
include the plural number. The word "shall" is always mandatory and not merely
directory.
BULK WATER HAULING: The transport of water away from the premises that water is
supplied to by the Mt. Pulaski water department.
CITY: The city of Mt. Pulaski.
COUNCIL: The city council of the city of Mt. Pulaski.
MAYOR: The mayor of the city of Mt. Pulaski.
PERSON: Any person, firm, partnership, association, corporation, company, or
organization of any kind.
WATER: Water supplied by the Mt. Pulaski water department either directly or
indirectly to another entity. (Ord., 7-24-2012)
8-10-3: WATER SERVICE EMERGENCY DECLARED BY THE MAYOR:
Whenever, upon determination by the mayor of the city of Mt. Pulaski, in
consultation with such officials as he deems appropriate, the mayor of the city
determines that a water service emergency exists in the city of Mt. Pulaski,
and that such emergency requires that certain uses of water not essential to
the health, welfare and safety of the citizens of the city be restricted and
the mayor issues and publishes and posts a declaration of such findings, in a
local newspaper of general publication, the provisions of this chapter shall
become immediately effective and applicable to all persons or entities served
by the Mt. Pulaski water system.
Further, prior to enacting a stage of water restriction, the mayor shall cause
to be posted at city hall, the post office, the city website, by mass e-mail to
those individuals or entities signed up through city hall on the city's e-mail
list, and at any other place deemed appropriate, notice of the stage of water
restriction in effect along with the date and time of posting. The stage of
water restriction shall take effect twenty four (24) hours after posting of the
notice. Once the mayor has declared a water service emergency, it is the
responsibility of the city water customers to inform themselves of the current
stage of water restriction. Failure of the city to post notice as described due
to circumstances beyond their control is not a defense for water customers
failing to abide by the restrictions. The notice may be posted at other
locations and through other means deemed appropriate.
It is not necessary that the stages of water restriction progress one step at a
time. The mayor may declare any stage to be in effect at any time that is
deemed appropriate and necessary. (Ord., 7-24-2012)
8-10-4: STAGES OF WATER RESTRICTION:
It shall be unlawful to use water delivered by the Mt. Pulaski water system in
violation of the following stages of restriction:
Stage 1: The mayor may request that the city water customers voluntarily reduce
         water usage in order to prevent the need for mandatory restrictions.
Stage 2: All bulk water hauling is prohibited, except fighting a fire in
         progress.
Stage 3: Stage 2 activities and the following activities are prohibited:
        Filling of swimming pools except kid size pools limited to one hundred
         (100) gallons.
        Washing of any pavement, driveway, or building.
        Washing of any vehicle except at commercial car wash facilities.
        Watering of ball fields.
        Watering of gardens except by use of hand operated nozzles.
        Watering of yards.
Stage 4: Stage 2 and stage 3 activities and the following activities are
         prohibited:
        Filling of swimming pools of any size.
        The following also applies:
        Water flow to all commercial users outside the city limits shall be
         restricted except nursing home use and firefighting use.
Stage 5: Stage 2, stage 3 and stage 4 activities are prohibited and the
         following also apply:
        Water flow to any commercial water user outside the city limits shall
         be shut off except nursing home use and firefighting use.
Stage 6: Stage 2, stage 3, and stage 4 activities are prohibited; stage 5 and
         the following also apply:
        Water flow to any water user outside the city limits shall be shut off
         except nursing home use and firefighting use.
Stage 7: Stage 2, stage 3, and stage 4 activities are prohibited; stage 5 and
         stage 6 and the following also apply:
         Water to city users shall be shut off for periods of time as
        determined by the mayor in consultation with the water department.
         Twenty four (24) hour notice requirements do not apply to this stage.
 
(Ord., 7-24-2012)
8-10-5: FINES AND PENALTIES:
Any violation of this chapter shall be penalized in accordance with section
1-4-1, "General Penalty", of this code, except for stage 2 violations which
shall be penalized as follows:
First offense: Two hundred fifty dollars ($250.00).
Second offense: Five hundred dollars ($500.00) plus restriction of water flow
until declaration of water emergency has been lifted.
Third offense: Elimination of water service until declaration of water
emergency has been lifted. (Ord., 7-24-2012)

TRAFFIC REGULATIONS

SECTION:
9-1-1: Traffic Code Adopted
9-1-1: TRAFFIC CODE ADOPTED:
There is hereby adopted for the purpose of prescribing regulations for
pedestrians and the operation of vehicles, that certain code known as the
Illinois vehicle code, 625 Illinois Compiled Statutes, as amended, which code
has been and now is filed in the office of the city clerk, and the same is
hereby adopted and represented as fully as if set out at length herein, and the
provisions thereof shall be controlling within the limits of the city. (1977
Code)

SPEED RESTRICTIONS
SECTION:

9-2-1: SPEED LIMITS ESTABLISHED:
The speed limit for motor vehicles on all public streets within the limits of
the city shall be twenty five (25) miles per hour unless otherwise posted.
(Ord., 7-25-1989; amd. 2010 Code)

9-3-2: ANGLE PARKING:
   A.   The city council is authorized to mark or sign such streets within the
city on which angle parking shall be permitted.
   B.   On such streets where angle parking shall be permitted, including
streets around the City Square so designated and marked, vehicles shall be
parked at an approximate forty five degree (45°) angle with the curb. The city
shall cause the surface of said designated streets to be marked in such a
manner as to set off spaces or boundary lines within which vehicles may be
parked at an angle. It shall be unlawful to park any vehicle across any such
line or mark, or to park such vehicle in a way that the same shall not be fully
within the area so designated by such lines or markings.
   C.   Nothing contained in this section shall prevent trucks from parking on
the centerline of the streets around the City Square for the purpose of loading
and unloading. (Ord., 6-23-1970)

a specified period of time when the disability is temporary as certified by the
physician.

be displayed in the lower left portion of the rear window of the vehicle in

The driver of a vehicle shall stop at the entrance to a through street and
shall yield the right of way to other vehicles which have entered the
intersection or which are approaching so close on a through street as to
constitute an immediate hazard, unless directed otherwise by the traffic
officer or a traffic control signal. (1967 Code § 18.201)

as one-way streets or alleys by ordinance, in any direction other than that so
designated. (1967 Code § 18.202)

Street and Vine Street shall be limited to one-way traffic for vehicles going
south. (Ord., 1-27-1981)
   B.   In front of Mt. Pulaski Grade School, a section of Garden Street from
Jefferson Street to Morgan Street shall be limited to one-way traffic for
vehicles going north. (Ord., 2-8-2000; amd. per minutes dated 5-10-2005)

9-4-4: YIELD RIGHT OF WAY STREETS:
Any street designated by ordinance as a yield right of way street and so posted
is hereby declared to be a yield right of way street.
The driver of a vehicle in obedience to a yield right of way sign shall reduce
the speed of his vehicle to not more than twenty (20) miles per hour and shall
yield the right of way to other vehicles which have entered the intersecting
street either from the right or left or which are approaching so closely on
such intersection as to constitute a hazard, but said driver having so yielded
may proceed at such time as a safe interval occurs.
If a driver is involved in a collision at an intersection or interferes with
the movement of other vehicles after driving past a yield right of way sign,
such collision shall be deemed prima facie evidence of the driver's failure to
yield the right of way. (1967 Code § 18.204)
The following intersections are hereby established as yield right of way
intersections, and traffic moving from the first street named to the second
street named shall yield the right of way as required by this chapter:

9-4-6: POSTING SIGNS:
The chief of the police department shall post or cause to be posted suitable
signs for all through streets, one-way streets or alleys, stop intersections
and yield right of way streets. (1967 Code § 18.205)
9-4-7: PENALTY:
Any person violating the provisions of this chapter shall be subject to the
penalty under the provisions of section
1-4-1 of this code for each offense. (1977 Code)
CHAPTER 5
BICYCLES
SECTION:
9-5-1: Scope Of Chapter
9-5-2: Traffic Laws Apply To Riders
9-5-3: Mechanical Condition
9-5-4: Equipment Required
9-5-5: Rules Of Operation
9-5-1: SCOPE OF CHAPTER:
   A.   It shall be unlawful for any person to do any act forbidden or fail to
perform any act required in this chapter.
   B.   The parent of any child or the guardian of any ward shall not authorize
or knowingly permit any such child or ward to violate any of the provisions of
this chapter.
   C.   The regulations applicable to bicycles shall apply whenever any bicycle
is operated upon any highway or upon any path set aside for the exclusive use
of bicycles subject to those exceptions stated herein. (1977 Code)
9-5-2: TRAFFIC LAWS APPLY TO RIDERS:
Every person riding a bicycle upon a roadway shall be subject to the provisions
of this title, except as changed by special regulations contained in this
chapter and those provisions of this title which, by their nature, can have no
application. (1977 Code)
9-5-3: MECHANICAL CONDITION:
All police officers shall have authority to inspect all bicycles for mechanical
fitness. (1977 Code)
9-5-4: EQUIPMENT REQUIRED:
   A.   Brakes: Every bicycle, when operated upon a highway, shall be equipped
with a brake adequate to control the movement of and to stop such bicycle
whenever necessary. (1977 Code)
   B.   Lamps And Reflectors: Every bicycle operated after sunset shall be
equipped with a lamp on the front exhibiting a white light visible from a
distance of at least five hundred feet (500') to the front and with a red
reflector on the rear. Every such reflector shall be so designed and maintained
as to be visible at night from all distances from one hundred feet (100') to
six hundred feet (600') to the rear from such bicycle when directly in front of
a motor vehicle displaying lawful lower beams of headlamps. A lamp exhibiting a
red light visible from a distance of five hundred feet (500') to the rear may
be used in addition to the rear reflector.
   C.   Audible Signal: No bicycle shall be equipped with nor shall any person
use upon a bicycle any siren or whistle. This provision does not apply to a
bicycle that is a police vehicle. (1977 Code; amd. 2010 Code)
9-5-5: RULES OF OPERATION:
   A.   Riding On Bicycles:
      1.   A person propelling a bicycle shall not ride other than upon the
permanent and regular seat attached thereto, nor carry any other person upon
such bicycle other than upon a firmly attached and regular seat thereon,
except, that an adult rider may carry a child securely attached to the person
in a backpack or sling; nor shall any person ride upon a bicycle other than as
authorized in this subsection A1. (1977 Code; amd. 2010 Code)
      2.   No bicycle shall be used to carry more persons at one time than the
number for which it is designed and equipped.
   B.   Right Of Way On Sidewalks: When permitted or required by this chapter
to ride on sidewalks, bicycle riders shall use the right side of sidewalks
insofar as practicable. A person riding a bicycle on a sidewalk shall yield the
right of way to every pedestrian and, when approaching a pedestrian from the
rear, shall give audible warning signal when at least twenty five feet (25')
distant from the pedestrian.
   C.   Speed Of Bicycles: No person riding a bicycle shall ride faster than is
reasonable and proper in regard to the safety of the rider and others.
   D.   Clinging To Vehicles: No person riding upon any bicycle shall hold onto
or cling to another vehicle powered by a motor. (1977 Code)
   E.   Carrying Articles: No person riding a bicycle shall carry any package,
bundle or article which prevents the use of both hands in the control and
operation of the bicycle. A person operating a bicycle shall keep at least one
hand on the handlebars at all times. (1977 Code; amd. 2010 Code)
   F.   Trick Riding: No rider of a bicycle shall remove both hands from the
handlebars, or feet from the pedals, or practice any acrobatic or fancy riding
on any street; nor shall any person operating a bicycle upon a public highway
participate in any race for speed or endurance contest with any other vehicle,
except under permit from and under the supervision of the police department.
   G.   Parking Bicycles: No person shall park a bicycle in such a manner as to
interfere with pedestrians or persons getting into or out of vehicles. (1977
Code)
CHAPTER 6
VIOLATIONS; PENALTIES
SECTION:
9-6-1: Parking Violations
9-6-2: Unauthorized Use Of Parking Spaces For Persons With Disabilities
9-6-3: Restrictions On Noise
9-6-4: Penalty
9-6-1: PARKING VIOLATIONS:
Any person accused of a violation of an ordinance prohibiting parking in
certain designated areas, or restricting the length of time a vehicle may be
parked, may settle and compromise such claim against him or her for such
illegal parking by paying to the city:
   A.   The sum of ten dollars ($10.00) if paid within seventy two (72) hours
of the time such alleged offense was committed. (Ord., 10-9-2001)
   B.   Fines paid after seventy two (72) hours but within five (5) days of the
date of the traffic violation ticket shall carry an additional fifty percent
(50%) penalty fee.
   C.   If the fine is not paid within five (5) days of the date of the traffic
ticket, a warrant of arrest for such violator, or the registered owner of such
vehicle, shall be obtained and issued through the city attorney. (Ord., 5-22-
1979)
   D.   The minimum fine of ten dollars ($10.00) for parking violations shall
not apply: (Ord., 5-22-1979; amd. Ord., 10-9-2001)
      1.   For parking any vehicle within fifteen feet (15') of a fire hydrant;
or
      2.   For parking any vehicle in the wrong direction, either by back-in
parking in a diagonal parking space or by parking on the wrong side of the
street in a parallel parking space. (Ord., 5-22-1979)
The sum of ten dollars ($10.00) shall be the minimum fine for a violation of
either subsection D1 or D2 of this section. Failure to pay such fine within the
time periods set forth in subsections A, B and C of this section shall result
in the additional penalties and sanctions as therein set forth. (Ord., 5-22-
1979; amd. 2010 Code)
Payment of any fine hereunder shall be made at the police station or at the
city hall. A receipt shall be issued for all monies so received, and said
monies shall be promptly turned over to the city treasurer.
When such payment has been made, the members of the police department are
hereby authorized to refrain from instituting a prosecution for the alleged
offense involved.
Provided, that this section shall not apply to persons parking a vehicle so as
to obstruct the entrance or exit of any place where police or fire department
apparatus or other emergency equipment is kept or housed, or so as to block an
emergency entrance in a hospital. Nor shall this section apply to any person
charged with parking a vehicle so as to entirely obstruct traffic on any street
or alley, or parking in such a way as to reduce traffic on an arterial street
to one-way traffic only; nor to any person who refuses to move a vehicle
illegally parked at the request of any member of the police department. (Ord.,
5-24-1976)
9-6-2: UNAUTHORIZED USE OF PARKING SPACES FOR PERSONS WITH DISABILITIES:
Any person violating the provisions of section
9-3-5, "Parking Spaces Reserved For Persons With Disabilities", of this title
shall be guilty of a petty offense and shall be fined fifty dollars ($50.00)
for each offense. (Ord., 4-9-1985; amd. 2010 Code)
9-6-3: RESTRICTIONS ON NOISE:
No radio, tape, cassette or other recording shall be operated in a home or in a
private pleasure vehicle in such a manner that the noise therefrom is audible
at a distance of fifty feet (50') or more from such vehicle or home. This
section shall not apply to noise devices, bands or other musical devices used
in any public parade or procession which is operated under a permit in
accordance with the ordinances of the city. Excessive noise due to muffler or
tires on any type of motor driven vehicle shall be construed to be a violation
of this section. (Ord., 4-8-1986)
9-6-4: PENALTY:
Unless otherwise provided, any person violating any provision of this title
shall be guilty of a petty offense and shall be fined not less than seventy
five dollars ($75.00) nor more than seven hundred fifty dollars ($750.00) for
each offense. The fine shall be paid at city hall. A receipt shall be issued
for all monies so received, and said monies shall be promptly turned over to
the city treasurer. (Ord., 4-8-1986; amd. 2010 Code)
CHAPTER 7
TRUCK TRAFFIC
SECTION:
9-7-1: Through Truck Traffic Prohibited
9-7-2: Left Turn Prohibited
9-7-1: THROUGH TRUCK TRAFFIC PROHIBITED:
   A.   It shall be unlawful to drive or tow any semitractor and trailer upon
the city streets.
   B.   Truck drivers living in the city or truck drivers making local
deliveries are exempt. Bills of lading or vehicle registration shall be used to
determine exemption.
   C.   The fine for violating this section shall be fifty dollars ($50.00) for
the first offense and one hundred dollars ($100.00) for each offense
thereafter. (Ord., 6-23-1987)
9-7-2: LEFT TURN PROHIBITED:
Through truck traffic is prohibited from turning left off of Chestnut Street
onto Route 121. (Ord., 2-8-2000)
CHAPTER 8
SNOWMOBILES
SECTION:
9-8-1: Definitions
9-8-2: Obedience To Police
9-8-3: Registration Required
9-8-4: Equipment
9-8-5: Operation
9-8-6: Routes
9-8-7: Times Of Operation
9-8-8: Regulations
9-8-9: Emergencies
9-8-10: Penalties
9-8-1: DEFINITIONS:
The definitions set forth in the snowmobile registration and safety act of the
state, 625 Illinois Compiled Statutes 40/1-1 et seq., hereinafter called the
"act", as amended, are hereby incorporated herein by reference and made a part
hereof. (Ord., 3-28-1995)
9-8-2: OBEDIENCE TO POLICE:
Police officers are hereby authorized to direct all snowmobile traffic in
accordance with the provisions of this title, or in emergencies as public
safety or convenience may require, and it shall be unlawful for any person to
fail or refuse to comply with any lawful order, signal or directions of a
police officer. Except in an emergency, it shall be unlawful for any person not
authorized by law to direct or attempt to direct snowmobile traffic. (Ord., 3-
28-1995)
9-8-3: REGISTRATION REQUIRED:
No person shall operate any snowmobile within the corporate limits of the city
unless such snowmobile has been registered and numbered in accordance with the
act and unless the certificate or number awarded to such snowmobile is in full
force and effect and the identifying number set forth in the certificate is
displayed on each side of the cowling of such snowmobile in accordance with the
act, which is incorporated herein by reference and made a part hereof. (Ord.,
3-28-1995)
9-8-4: EQUIPMENT:
All snowmobiles operated within the corporate limits of the city shall be
equipped as required by the provisions of article IV of the act, which is
incorporated herein by reference and made a part hereof. (Ord., 3-28-1995)
9-8-5: OPERATION:
It is unlawful for any person to drive or operate any snowmobile in a manner
prohibited by article V of the act, which is incorporated herein by reference
and made a part hereof. (Ord., 3-28-1995)
9-8-6: ROUTES:
The following streets of the city shall be used as snowmobile routes for
ingress and egress to the city:
Vine Street from Flora Drive south to McDonald Street.
Spring Street east on Green Street to Washington Street, south on Washington
Street to McDonald Street, then east to Route 121.
Spring Street from the city limits north to Jasper Street.
Jasper Street from Spring Street east to Vine Street.
Chestnut Street from Vine Street east to the city limits.
Flora Drive from Vine Street northwesterly to Elkhart Road.
Elkhart Road west to Winter Street.
Winter Street south to Cooke Street.
Cooke Street from Winter Street east to Spring Street.
All operators of snowmobiles shall gain entry to the snowmobile route by the
most direct and accessible manner, without delay, from their homes to the
route. Any street of the city not designated as a snowmobile route shall be
used only by operators of snowmobiles for the purposes of traveling from their
homes to the routes and back. All persons operating snowmobiles on the routes
as above set forth will remain on or as close as possible to the right side of
the roadway and shall yield right of way to all other motor vehicles. (Ord., 3-
28-1995)
9-8-7: TIMES OF OPERATION:
Snowmobiles may be operated within the city as hereinabove provided, only
between the hours of seven o'clock (7:00) A.M. and twelve o'clock (12:00)
midnight each day of the week. No snowmobile may be operated within the city
between the hours of twelve o'clock (12:00) midnight and seven o'clock (7:00)
A.M. on any day. (Ord., 3-28-1995)
9-8-8: REGULATIONS:
In addition to the directions for operation of snowmobiles hereinabove set
forth, operators must obey all traffic regulations as prescribed for motor
vehicle traffic and are subject to penalties for violation thereof. (Ord., 3-
28-1995)
9-8-9: EMERGENCIES:
This chapter shall not be construed to prohibit the use of snowmobiles in the
city by authorized personnel of the city or of any other governmental body or
agency when said use shall be required for emergency purposes. (Ord., 3-28-
1995; amd. 2010 Code)
9-8-10: PENALTIES:
Any person convicted of violating any provision of this chapter shall be fined
at least twenty five dollars ($25.00), but not more than seven hundred fifty
dollars ($750.00). Any person convicted more than one time for violating this
chapter shall be fined not less than fifty dollars ($50.00) nor more than seven
hundred fifty dollars ($750.00) for each subsequent violation. (Ord., 3-28-
1995; amd. 2010 Code)
CHAPTER 9
GOLF CARTS
SECTION:
9-9-1: Definitions
9-9-2: Authorized Non-Highway Vehicles
9-9-3: City Permit And Inspection
9-9-4: Compliance With All Traffic Laws
9-9-5: Required Equipment
9-9-6: Rules And Regulations
9-9-7: Mandatory Insurance
9-9-8: Exceptions
9-9-9: Revocation Of Permit
9-9-10: Violations And Penalties
9-9-1: DEFINITIONS:
 
                          A vehicle specifically designed and intended for the
                          purposes of transporting one or more persons and
GOLF CART:                their golf clubs or maintenance equipment while
(taken from Sec. 1-123.9) engaged in the playing of golf, supervising the play
                          of golf, or maintaining the condition of the grounds
                          on a public or private golf course. (Ord. 10272020,
                          10-27-2020)
 
9-9-2: AUTHORIZED NON-HIGHWAY VEHICLES:
This ordinance restricts non-highway vehicles authorized for use to a “golf
cart” as set forth in this Chapter. (Ord. 10272020, 10-27-2020)
9-9-3: CITY PERMIT AND INSPECTION:
   A.   To be operated in the City of Mt. Pulaski pursuant to this Chapter, an
authorized non-highway vehicle shall be inspected and a permit issued by the
City of Mt. Pulaski. A person seeking a permit shall apply at city hall on
forms provided by the City. The completed application shall be maintained by
the city.
   B.   The permit shall be valid for one (1) year from the date of issuance.
   C.   Prior to the issuance of a permit an application and licensing fee of
fifty dollars ($50) shall be paid to the City Clerk.
   D.   Permit application must list all qualified persons who will be
operating the authorized non-highway vehicle. The serial number, make, model,
and description must also be provided.
   E.   The applicant and all listed operators must complete the Signed Waiver
of Liability releasing the city and agreeing to defend, indemnify and hold the
city harmless from any and all future claims resulting from the operation of
their authorized non-highway vehicle on city streets.
   F.   A photocopy of each operators Illinois drivers license and photocopy of
applicable liability insurance coverage specifically for the authorized non-
highway vehicle to be operated will be required.
   G.   The city retains the right to refuse to issue and/or revoke any permit
for any authorized non-highway vehicle at any time for any violation of this
subchapter or any other ordinance, rule, regulation or state or federal rule,
regulation or statute.
   H.   The applicant shall present the authorized non-highway vehicle to the
Chief of Police, or his designee, for an inspection to determine if it is
compliant with this ordinance and applicable state statutes. If the applicant
and vehicle are qualified, a permit shall be issued to the applicant that must
be conspicuously affixed to the rear of the vehicle that it may be easily
observed from the exterior. If a vehicle is sold, leased, or otherwise
transferred, the permit shall not be transferred or assigned to the buyer. A
buyer must apply for a permit in the manner provided above. (Ord. 10272020, 10-
27-2020)
9-9-4: COMPLIANCE WITH ALL TRAFFIC LAWS:
Authorized non-highway vehicles and passengers shall comply with all applicable
local and state traffic laws and ordinances. Violations may be ticketed and
prosecuted in the same manner as motor vehicle violations. (Ord. 10272020, 10-
27-2020)
9-9-5: REQUIRED EQUIPMENT:
To be operated in the City of Mt. Pulaski pursuant to this Chapter, an
authorized non-highway vehicle shall have the following equipment in good
working condition at all times:
   A.   Brakes;
   B.   A steering apparatus;
   C.   Tires for appropriate and reasonable use on city streets; a rear view
mirror;
   D.   Red reflectorized warning devices in the front and rear; a slow moving
emblem as required by 625 ILCS 5/12-709 in plain view on the rear of the golf
cart;
   E.    A head light that emits a white light visible from 500 feet to the
front;
   F.   A tail lamp that emits a red light visible from at least 100 feet from
the rear;
   G.   Brake lights on the rear; and
   H.   Turn signals on the front and rear. (Ord. 10272020, 10-27-2020)
9-9-6: RULES AND REGULATIONS:
   A.   To be operated in the City of Mt. Pulaski pursuant to this Chapter, an
authorized non-highway vehicle shall have its headlight and tail lamps
illumined at all times.
   B.   No person shall operate an authorized non-highway vehicle in the City
of Mt. Pulaski unless the operator is at least eighteen years of age (18) and
has a valid Illinois driver’s license.
   C.   An authorized non-highway vehicle may only be operated commencing at
sunrise and ending at sunset with the times being those reported by the
national weather service for the Springfield, Illinois area. An authorized non-
highway vehicle may not be operated when visibility is impaired by weather,
smoke, fog, or other conditions or at any time when there is insufficient light
to clearly see persons and vehicles on the roadway at a distance of 500 feet.
   D.   No authorized non-highway vehicle shall be operated with more occupants
or passengers than its factory-installed seating provides.
   E.   No authorized non-highway vehicle shall tow, haul, or trailer any
device or equipment on any city street.
   F.   Each driver and passenger of a golf cart shall wear a properly fastened
and adjusted seat safety belt. Children must be secured in a child restraint
system as required pursuant to the Child Passenger Protection Act (625 ILCS 25/
1 et seq.).
   G.   Authorized non-highway vehicles shall have no increased power,
wheelbase, seating or tire modifications from a standard manufactured vehicle.
   H.   Operation on Vine Street is prohibited except between Maple Street and
Flora Drive. Operation of an authorized non-highway vehicle shall not be
permitted on any city sidewalk, Illinois Route 121 or County Route 10 (Elkhart
Road). Crossing Illinois Route 121 and County Route 10 in a straight line only
is permitted.
   I.   Open alcohol is prohibited while operating non-highway vehicle. Any
person who drives or is in actual physical control of a non-highway vehicle on
a roadway while under the influence is subject to 625 Illinois Compiled
Statutes 5/11-501 through 5/11-502 of the Illinois Vehicle Code. (Ord.
10272020, 10-27-2020)
9-9-7: MANDATORY INSURANCE:
No person in the City of Mt. Pulaski shall operate, or permit another person to
operate, an authorized non-highway vehicle unless the operator is covered by a
liability insurance policy as required by 625 ILCS 5/7-601 of the Illinois
Vehicle Code; and the operator carries with him proof of liability insurance as
required by 625 ILCS 5/7-602 of the Illinois Vehicle Code. (Ord. 10272020, 10-
27-2020)
9-9-8: EXCEPTIONS:
Exceptions for use of non-highway vehicles not listed or defined in this
chapter may be granted by the Mayor, Chief of Police, or his designee for
public works employees or other authorized personnel during city events or
festivities. (Ord. 10272020, 10-27-2020)
9-9-9: REVOCATION OF PERMIT:
   A.   A permit to operate an authorized non-highway vehicle may be revoked by
the Chief of Police, or his designee, if:
      1.   There is any material misrepresentation made by the applicant on the
application; or
      2.   The required liability insurance is no longer in full force and
effect; or
      3.   It has been determined that the operator can no longer safely
operate the vehicle; or it has been determined that the vehicle cannot be
safely operated; the vehicle fails to meet the standard equipment requirements
set forth herein; or
      4.   Upon a finding that the holder of the permit has violated any of the
provisions of this chapter or the Illinois vehicle code or for any reason that
the Chief of Police or his designee feels is appropriate to ensure the safety
and well-being of the citizens of the City.
   B.   The Chief of Police, or his designee, shall issue a Notice of
Revocation of the permit and serve it upon the license holder personally either
verbally or in written form or by certified mail at the address provided in the
license application. The revocation shall go into effect immediately after
personal service or on the third day after the postmark of the certified mail
receipt.
   C.   No person with a revoked permit shall be eligible to reapply for a
permit for a period of one (1) year following the revocation.
   D.   An appeal for a revocation may be made directly to the City Council and
heard either at a regularly noticed or special meeting. (Ord. 10272020, 10-27-
2020)
9-9-10: VIOLATIONS AND PENALTIES:
   A.   Any person found in violation of the provisions of this Ordinance may
be ticketed no less than one hundred fifty dollars ($ 150) per offense plus any
additional court and collection costs.
   B.   For purposes of this subsection, separate occurrences for the same
violation of the Ordinance constitutes a separate offense. (Ord. 10272020, 10-
27-2020)
TITLE 10
ZONING REGULATIONS
CHAPTER 1
OFFICIAL CITY PLAN
SECTION:
10-1-1: Establishment
10-1-2: Reference
10-1-3: Compliance
10-1-1: ESTABLISHMENT:
The official plan of the city, approved by the city council, shall consist of
the following:
   A.   A map of the city, charts and diagrams showing proposed additions to
and improvements of the city streets, parks, public buildings, sewage disposal
system, water system and street lighting system. (1967 Code § 10.301; amd. 2010
Code)
   B.   The specifications for street construction and paving established by
the city council.
   C.   The zoning ordinance.
   D.   The subdivision control ordinance. (1967 Code § 10.301)
10-1-2: REFERENCE:
Any reference to the official plan of the city shall be taken to mean and
include all of the enactments set out in section
10-1-1 of this chapter. (1967 Code § 10.302)
10-1-3: COMPLIANCE:
No plat of subdivision, plan for the construction or layout of streets, or work
involving laying sewer or water mains shall be approved unless the same
complies fully with the requirements of the city plan. (1967 Code § 10.303)
CHAPTER 2
GENERAL ZONING PROVISIONS
SECTION:
10-2-1: Title
10-2-2: Purpose
10-2-3: Intent
10-2-4: Abrogation And Greater Restrictions
10-2-5: Interpretation
10-2-6: Severability
10-2-7: Jurisdiction
10-2-8: Restrictions
10-2-9: Site Restrictions
10-2-1: TITLE:
This title shall be known, cited and referred to as the MT. PULASKI, ILLINOIS,
ZONING ORDINANCE. (Ord., 8-24-1974)
10-2-2: PURPOSE:
This title is adopted for the following purposes:
   A.   To promote and protect the public health, safety, morals, comfort and
general welfare of the people;
   B.   To divide the city into zones or districts restricting and regulating
therein the location, erection, construction, reconstruction, alteration and
use of buildings, structures and land for residential, business and other
specified uses;
   C.   To protect the character and the stability of the residential, business
and manufacturing areas within the city, and to promote the orderly and
beneficial development of such areas;
   D.   To provide adequate light, air, privacy and convenience of access to
property;
   E.   To regulate the intensity of use of lot areas, and to determine the
area of open spaces surrounding buildings necessary to provide adequate light
and air, and to protect the public health;
   F.   To establish building lines and the location of buildings designed for
residential, business, manufacturing or other uses within such areas;
   G.   To fix reasonable standards to which buildings or structures shall
conform;
   H.   To prohibit uses, buildings or structures incompatible with the
character of development or intended uses within specified zoning districts;
   I.   To prevent additions to or remodeling of existing buildings or
structures in such a way as to avoid the restrictions and limitations imposed
hereunder:
      1.   To limit congestion in the public streets and protect the public
health, safety, convenience and general welfare by providing for the off street
parking of motor vehicles and the loading of commercial vehicles;
      2.   To protect against fire, explosion, noxious fumes and other hazards
in the interest of the public health, safety, comfort and general welfare;
      3.   To prevent the overcrowding of land and undue concentration of
structures, so far as is possible and appropriate, in each district by
regulating the use and bulk of buildings in relation to the land surrounding
them;
      4.   To conserve the taxable value of land and buildings throughout the
city;
      5.   To provide for the elimination of nonconforming uses of land,
buildings and structures which are adversely affecting the character and value
of desirable development in each district; and
      6.   To define and limit the powers and duties of the administrative
officers and bodies as provided herein. (Ord., 8-24-1974)
10-2-3: INTENT:
It shall be the intent of this title to divide the city into districts for the
purpose of classifying, regulating and restricting the location of trades,
industries and commercial enterprises, and the location of buildings arranged,
intended and designed for specified uses; of regulating and limiting the height
and bulk of buildings hereafter erected; of classifying, regulating and
determining the area of front, rear and side yards, courts and other open
spaces about buildings; and of regulating and limiting the intensity of the use
of land and lot areas within the city. (Ord., 8-24-1974)
10-2-4: ABROGATION AND GREATER RESTRICTIONS:
   A.   Where the conditions imposed by any provision of this title upon the
use of land or buildings or upon the bulk of buildings are either more
restrictive or less restrictive than comparable conditions imposed by any other
provision of this title, or any other law, ordinance, resolution, rule or
regulation of any kind, the regulations which are more restrictive (or which
impose higher standards or requirements) shall govern.
   B.   This title is not intended to abrogate any easement, covenant or any
other private agreement; provided, that where the regulations of this title are
more restrictive (or impose higher standards or requirements), then the
provisions of this title shall govern. (Ord., 8-24-1974)
10-2-5: INTERPRETATION:
In their interpretation and application, the provisions of this title shall be
held to be the minimum requirements for the promotion of the public health,
safety, morals and welfare. (Ord., 8-24-1974)
10-2-6: SEVERABILITY:
If any section, clause, provision or portion of this title is adjudged
unconstitutional or invalid by a court of competent jurisdiction, the remainder
of this title shall not be affected thereby. (Ord., 8-24-1974)
10-2-7: JURISDICTION:
The jurisdiction of this title shall include all lands and waters within the
corporate limits of the city, and all land and waters in sections 10, 11, 12,
13, 14, 15, 22, 23, 24 of the northeast quarter of section 27, the northern
half of section 26, and the northwest quarter of section 25 of the township of
Mt. Pulaski, Logan County, Illinois. All buildings erected hereafter, all uses
of land or buildings established hereafter, and all structural alterations or
relocation of existing buildings occurring hereafter shall be subject to all
regulations of this title, which are applicable to the zoning districts in
which such buildings, uses or land shall be located. (Ord., 12-23-1975)
10-2-8: RESTRICTIONS:
   A.   Only those principal and accessory uses specified for a district shall
be permitted in that district.
   B.   Accessory uses and structures are permitted in any district, but not
until their principal structure is present or under construction.
   C.   Conditional uses and their accessory uses are permitted in districts as
specified, but only according to the conditional use procedure in chapter 12 of
this title.
   D.   In case of uncertainty where the zoning enforcement officer is unable
to determine literally whether a use is permitted as a principal or accessory
use, he shall consult the board of zoning appeals 1  for an original
interpretation.
   E.   Temporary uses such as real estate sales field offices or shelters for
materials and equipment being used in the construction of a permanent structure
are permitted while sales or construction is in progress. (Ord., 8-24-1974)
 
Notes
1 1. See title 2, chapter 1 of this code.
10-2-9: SITE RESTRICTIONS:
   A.   All lots shall abut upon a public thoroughfare with at least thirty
feet (30') of frontage unless a variance or planned development project is
approved.
   B.   Only one principal structure shall be located, erected or moved onto
any lot or parcel of land.
   C.   No zoning permit shall be issued for a lot which abuts a public street
dedicated to only a portion of its proposed width, and located on that side
thereof for which the required dedication has not been secured.
   D.   No lot, yard, parking area, building area or other space shall be
reduced in area or dimension so as not to meet the provisions of this title. No
part of any lot, yard, parking area or other space required for a structure or
use shall be used for any other structure or use.
   E.   Any lot in a single ownership, which ownership was of record at the
effective date hereof, that does not meet the requirements of this title for
yards, courts or other area of open space may be utilized for single residence
purposes; provided, the requirements for such yard or court area, width, depth
or open space is within seventy five percent (75%) of that required by the
terms of this title. The purpose of this subsection is to permit utilization of
recorded lots which lack adequate width or depth as long as reasonable living
standards can be provided. (Ord., 8-24-1974)
   F.   No wall, fence or hedge more than four feet (4') in height shall be
permitted in the front yard or side yard abutting a public street. Every wall,
fence or hedge shall be constructed or planted in such a manner that it can be
maintained by the owner or owners without trespassing on the abutting property.
Every wall, fence or hedge shall be set back not less than eighteen inches
(18") from the abutting property line. The decorative side of the fence shall
be facing toward the abutting neighbor's property. (Ord., 11-14-1989)
   G.   No wall, fence or hedge which would obstruct motor vehicle visibility
of traffic approaching the corner or intersection shall be erected, placed or
maintained within a triangular area formed by the intersecting lot lines
nearest the street intersection and a straight line joining said lot lines at
points which are thirty feet (30') distant from the point of intersecting lot
lines 1 .
   H.   The space in any minimum required yard shall be open and unobstructed
except for the ordinary projections of windowsills, belt courses, eaves, roof
overhangs and other architectural features of residential properties; provided,
however, that such features do not project closer than three feet (3') from the
side lot lines. (Ord., 8-24-1974)
   I.   Any accessory building shall be at least five feet (5') from the side
lot line and five feet (5') from the rear lot line; provided, however, where
the accessory building is a private garage used to store one or more passenger
motor vehicles or trucks of three-fourths (3/4) ton or less, access to which
garage is by a public alley only, then the private garage shall be at least
twenty feet (20') from the rear lot line. (Ord., 3-27-1990)
   J.   All overhanging canopies, marquees, awnings and similar structures must
be at least eight feet (8') above a sidewalk at any point, and overhanging
signs must be a minimum of ten feet (10') above the sidewalk at any point. Such
structures cannot project nearer than one foot (1') from any driveway 2 .
(Ord., 8-24-1974; amd. 1977 Code)
   K.   The minimum setback from any portion of a lot bordering a public street
shall be the same as the required front setback for that district. (Ord., 8-24-
1974)
   L.   No satellite receiver dish antennas or microwave receiver dish antennas
shall be permitted in the front yard or side yard abutting a public street, or
be erected, placed or maintained in a manner that would obstruct motor vehicle
visibility of traffic approaching the corner or intersection within a
triangular area formed by the intersecting lot lines nearest the street
intersection and a straight line joining said lot lines at points which are
thirty feet (30') distant from the point of intersecting lot lines 3 . (Ord.,
12-13-1988)

  8-4-5J and K of this code.

CHAPTER 3
ZONING DEFINITIONS
SECTION:
10-3-1: Rules And Definitions
10-3-1: RULES AND DEFINITIONS:
   A.   Words used in the present tense shall include the future, and words
used in the singular number shall include the plural number, and the plural the
singular, where the context requires.
   B.   The word "may" is permissive.
   C.   The word "shall" is mandatory and not discretionary.
   D.   The word "lot" shall include the words "piece", "parcel" and "tract",
and the phrase "used for" shall include the phrases "arranged for", "assigned
for", "maintained for" and "occupied for".
   E.   All measured distances shall be to the nearest integral foot; if a
fraction is one-half foot (1/2') or less, the integral foot next below shall be
taken.
   F.   Any word not defined in this section shall be construed in its general
accepted meaning, as defined in the most recent publication of Webster's
Dictionary.
   G.   The words and terms set forth in this section, wherever they occur in
this title, shall be interpreted as herein defined.
ACCESSORY BUILDING: A subordinate building or structure attached to or detached
from the main building located in and occupying more than thirty percent (30%)
of the rear yard adjoining the main building, the use of which is incidental to
that of the main building. No accessory building shall be constructed unless
and until the main building has been erected on the premises.
BOARDING HOUSE (ROOMING OR LODGING HOUSE): A residential building or portion
thereof, other than a motel, apartment hotel or hotel, containing lodging rooms
for accommodations of three (3) or more persons who are not members of the
keeper's family, and where lodging or meals, or both, are provided by
prearrangement and for definite periods, at a definite prearranged price.
BUILDING: Any structure having a roof supported by columns or walls used or
intended to be used for the shelter or enclosure of persons, animals,
equipment, machinery or materials.
BUILDING HEIGHT: The vertical distance measured from the mean elevation of the
finished lot grade along the front yard face of the structure to the highest
point of flat roofs; to the mean height level between the eaves and ridges of
gable, hip and pitch roofs; or to the deck line of mansard roofs.
COMPREHENSIVE PLAN: The extensively developed and evolving plan, also called a
master plan, adopted by the planning commission 1 .
CONSERVATION: Preservation of land, water, flora, fauna and cultural artifacts
in their original state.
CONSUMER SERVICE: Sale of any service to individual customers for their own
personal benefit, enjoyment or convenience. For example, consumer services
include the provision of personal services such as beautician and barbering
services, the provision of lodging, entertainment, specialized instruction,
financial services, transportation, laundry and dry cleaning services, and all
other similar services.
DWELLING: A building designated for residential living purposes and containing
one or more dwelling units and/or lodging units.
DWELLING, MULTI-FAMILY: A dwelling containing three (3) or more dwelling units.
DWELLING, SINGLE-FAMILY: A dwelling containing one dwelling unit.
DWELLING, TWO-FAMILY: A dwelling containing two (2) dwelling units with one
dwelling unit arranged on the same story or stories above the other dwelling
unit.
DWELLING UNIT: One or more rooms constituting all or part of a dwelling which
are used exclusively as living quarters for one family and no more than two (2)
roomers or boarders, and which contain a stove, sink and other kitchen
facilities.
ESSENTIAL SERVICES: Services provided by public and private utilities necessary
for the exercise of the principal use or service of the principal structure.
These services include underground, surface or overhead gas, electrical, steam,
water, sanitary sewerage, stormwater drainage, and communication systems and
accessories thereto, such as poles, towers, wires, mains, drains, vaults,
culverts, laterals, sewers, pipes, catch basins, water storage tanks, conduits,
pumps, lift stations, hydrants, etc., but not including buildings.
FAMILY: Two (2) or more persons related to each other by blood, marriage or
legal adoption, living together as a single housekeeping unit; or a group of
not more than three (3) persons, who need not be related by blood, marriage or
legal adoption, living together as a single housekeeping unit and occupying a
single dwelling unit; in either case, exclusive of usual domestic servants.
FLOOR AREA: The sum of the gross floor area for each of the several stories
under a roof measured from the exterior limits or faces of a building or
structure. Areas below grade and attached accessory structures are not
included.
GARAGE, PRIVATE: An accessory building or an accessory portion of a principal
building enclosed on at least three (3) sides which is intended for and used to
store a private passenger motor vehicle, and no more than one three-fourths (3/
4) ton or lesser sized truck.
GRADE: The highest level of the finished surface of the ground adjacent to the
exterior walls of the building or structure.
HOME OCCUPATION, PROFESSIONAL: Any business or profession carried on by a
member of the immediate family residing on the premises, in connection with
which: a) there are no signs, other than a permitted nameplate when attached to
a principal building, and no activity that will indicate from the exterior that
the building is being used in whole or in part for any purpose other than that
of dwelling; b) there are no commodities sold or services rendered that require
receipt and delivery of merchandise, goods or equipment by other than a
passenger motor vehicle, or by first class mail; and c) no one outside the home
may be employed.
JUNKYARD: Any land or structure used for salvaging operations including, among
other things, the storage and sale of wastepaper, rags, scrap metal and
discarded materials, and the collecting, dismantling, storage and salvaging of
unlicensed, inoperative vehicles.
LIGHT INDUSTRY: Light industrial, office and administrative offices having few,
if any, adverse effects on neighboring properties. All processing and storage
shall take place within completely enclosed buildings.
LOADING AREA: A completely off street space or berth on the same lot for the
loading and unloading of freight carriers having adequate ingress and egress to
a public street or alley.
LODGING ROOM: A room rented as sleeping and living quarters, but without
cooking facilities, and with or without an individual bathroom. In a suite of
rooms, each room providing sleeping accommodations shall be counted as one
lodging room.
LOT: A single parcel of land which may be legally described as such or two (2)
or more adjacent numbered lots or parts of such lots in a recorded subdivision
plat having principal frontage on a street which comprises a site occupied by
or intended for occupancy by one principal building or principal use, together
with accessory buildings and uses, yards and other open spaces required by this
title.
LOT, CORNER: A lot abutting on two (2) streets at their juncture, when the
interior angle formed is less than one hundred thirty five degrees (135°).
LOT, INTERIOR: A lot other than a corner lot.
LOT LINES AND AREA: The peripheral boundaries of a parcel of land, and the
total area lying within such boundaries.
LOT, RECORDED: A lot designated on a subdivision plat or deed duly recorded
pursuant to statute in the county recorder's office. A recorded lot may not
coincide with a zoning lot.
LOT WIDTH: The width of a parcel of land measured at the rear of the specified
street yard.
LOT, ZONING: A parcel of land composed of one or more recorded lots occupied or
to be occupied by a principal building or buildings or principal use or uses
along with permitted accessory buildings or uses, meeting all the requirements
for area, building area, frontage, width, yards, setback and any other
requirements set forth in this title.
MOBILE HOME: A movable or portable unit designed and constructed to be
connected to utilities for year round occupancy and to provide complete,
independent living facilities including provisions for cooking, sleeping and
sanitation. The term includes units containing parts that may be collapsed or
telescoped when being towed and then be expanded to provide additional cubic
capacity, and units composed of two (2) or more separately towable components
being designed to be joined into an integral unit capable of being separated
again into components for repeated towing. Removal of wheels, towing devices or
any other alteration does not qualify a mobile home as a conventional single-
family dwelling unless such alterations enable it to meet the international
building code, 2006 edition.
MOTEL: An establishment consisting of a group of lodging rooms, each with
individual bathroom, and designed for use by transient guests. A motel
furnishes customary hotel services such as maid services and laundering of
linens used in the lodging rooms, telephone and secretarial or desk service,
and the use and upkeep of furniture.
NONCONFORMING STRUCTURE: A building or structure or portion thereof, lawfully
existing on the effective date hereof, which was designed, erected or
structurally altered for a use that does not conform to the use regulations of
the district in which it is located.
NONCONFORMING USE: A use which lawfully occupied a building or land on the
effective date hereof, and which does not conform with the use regulations of
the district in which it is located.
NONRETAIL COMMERCIAL: Commercial sales and services to customers who intend
resale of the products or merchandise sold or handled. For example, nonretail
commercial includes wholesale activities, warehousing, trucking terminals, and
similar commercial enterprises.
NURSING HOME OR REST HOME: A home for the aged, chronically ill or incurable
persons in which three (3) or more persons not of the immediate family are
received, kept or provided with food and shelter and care for compensation, but
not including hospitals, clinics or similar institutions devoted primarily to
the diagnosis, treatment or care of the sick or injured.
OPEN SALES LOT: Land used or occupied for the purpose of buying or selling
merchandise stored or displayed outside a building prior to sale. Such
merchandise includes, but is not limited to, passenger cars, trucks, motor
scooters, motorcycles, boats, monuments and trailers.
PARKING SPACE: A graded, all weather surface area of not less than two hundred
(200) square feet in area, either enclosed or open, for the parking of a motor
vehicle, having adequate ingress and egress to a public street or alley.
PERFORMANCE STANDARDS: Criteria established to control noise, odor, smoke,
particulate matter, toxic or noxious matter, vibration, fire and explosion
hazards or glare or heat generated by or inherent in uses of land or buildings.
PLANNED DEVELOPMENT: A parcel or tract of land initially under single ownership
or control, which contains two (2) or more principal buildings and one or more
principal uses, planned and constructed as a unified development.
RETAIL SALES: Sale of any product or merchandise to customers for their own
personal consumption or use, not for resale.
SANITARY LANDFILL: A method of disposing of refuse by spreading and covering
such refuse with earth to a depth of two feet (2') or more on the top surface
and one foot (1') or more on the sides of the bank.
SERVICE STATION, FILLING STATION, GAS STATION: Any building or premises which
is used for the dispensing, sale or offering for sale, at retail, of any motor
vehicle fuel or oils. Open storage shall be limited to no more than four (4)
vehicles stored for minor repair bearing current license plates. Such storage
shall not exceed seventy two (72) hours' duration and shall not permit the
storage of wrecked vehicles.
SETBACK, BUILDING: The minimum horizontal distance between the front lines of a
building or structure and the front lot lines.
SIGNS: Any words, letters, figures, numerals, phrases, sentences, emblems,
services, designs, trade names or trademarks by which information is made known
and which are used to advertise or promote an individual, firm, association,
corporation, profession, business, commodity or product, and which are visible
from any public street, highway or pedestrianway.
STRUCTURAL ALTERATIONS: Any change, other than incidental repairs, which would
prolong the life of the supporting members of a building or structure such as
bearing walls or partitions, columns, beams or girders; or any substantial
change in the roof or exterior walls.
STRUCTURE: Anything erected, the use of which requires more or less permanent
location on the ground or attached to something having a permanent location on
the ground. A sign, billboard or other advertising device detached or
projecting shall be construed to be a structure.
THOROUGHFARE: A street with a high degree of continuity which serves as an
intrastate, an intracounty or interstate highway, or as an arterial trafficway
between various major points of origin-destination. It affords a primary means
of access to abutting properties except from thoroughfares classified as
freeways or other limited access routes not containing frontage roads.
USE: The purpose or activity for which the land or building thereon is
designed, arranged or intended, or for which it is occupied or maintained.
USE, ACCESSORY: A use subordinate to the principal use and located on the same
premises serving a purpose customarily incidental to the principal use.
Residential accessory uses may include storage of household goods, parking
areas, gardening, servants' quarters, private swimming pools, private emergency
shelters, satellite receiver dish antennas and microwave receiver dish
antennas.
USE, CONDITIONAL: A use, either public or private, which, because of its unique
characteristics, cannot be properly classified as a permitted use in any
particular district or districts.
USE, PERMITTED: A use which may be lawfully established in a particular
district or districts, provided it conforms with all requirements, regulations
and performance standards, if any, of such district.
USE, PRINCIPAL: The main use of land or buildings as distinguished from a
subordinate or accessory use. It may be either a permitted or conditional use.
UTILITIES: Public and private facilities such as water wells, water and sewage
pumping stations, water storage tanks, power and communication transmission
lines, electrical power substations, static transformer stations, telephone and
telegraph exchanges, microwave radio relays, and gas regulation stations, but
not including sewage disposal plants, municipal incinerators, warehouses, shops
and storage yards.
YARD: An open space on a lot which is unoccupied and unobstructed from its
lowest level to the sky, except as otherwise provided in this title.
YARD, CORNER SIDE: A side yard which adjoins a street or thoroughfare.
YARD, FRONT (SETBACK): A yard which is bounded by the side lot lines, front lot
lines and the front yard line.
YARD, INTERIOR SIDE: A side yard which is located immediately adjacent to
another lot or to an alley separating such side yard from another lot.
YARD, REAR (SETBACK): A yard which is bounded by side lot lines, the rear lot
line and the rear yard line.
YARD, SIDE (SETBACK): A yard which is bounded by the rear yard line, front yard
line, side yard line and side lot line. (Ord., 8-24-1974; amd. 2010 Code)
 
Notes
1 1. See chapter 1 of this title.
CHAPTER 4
DISTRICTS AND MAP
SECTION:
10-4-1: Districts Established
10-4-2: Interpretation Of District Boundaries
10-4-3: Zoning Map
10-4-1: DISTRICTS ESTABLISHED:
For the purposes of this title, all land in the city, and all land and waters
in sections 10, 11, 12, 13, 14, 15, 22, 23, and 24, the northeast quarter of
section 27, the northern half of section 26, and the northwest quarter of
section 25 of the township of Mt. Pulaski, Logan County, Illinois, is hereby
divided into districts, as follows:
 
R-1 Residential district
B-1 General business district
B-2 Highway business district
M-1 Limited manufacturing district
M-2 General manufacturing district
A-1 Agricultural district
 
(Ord., 12-23-1975)
10-4-2: INTERPRETATION OF DISTRICT BOUNDARIES:
   A.   Boundaries of the zoning districts are hereby established as shown on
the map entitled "zoning map, Mt. Pulaski, Illinois", dated August 8, 1974, and
made a part of this title by reference. Such boundaries shall be construed to
follow: corporate limits; U.S. public land survey lines, lot or property lines;
centerlines of streets, highways, alleys, easements and railroad rights of way
or such lines extended; unless otherwise noted on the zoning map.
   B.   All land annexed to the city subsequent to the effective date hereof
shall be automatically made a part of the R-1 district unless the annexation
ordinance places the land in another district. (Ord., 8-24-1974)
10-4-3: ZONING MAP:
A certified copy of the zoning map shall be adopted and approved with the text
as part of this title, and shall be available to the public in the office of
the city clerk. (Ord., 8-24-1974)
CHAPTER 5
R-1 RESIDENTIAL DISTRICT
SECTION:
10-5-1: Purpose
10-5-2: Density Requirements
10-5-3: Number Of Structures Per Lot; Parking
10-5-4: Permitted Uses
10-5-5: Accessory Uses
10-5-6: Conditional Uses
10-5-1: PURPOSE:
The R-1 residential district is designed to provide an area for residential
uses and public and semipublic uses normally considered an integral part of the
area they serve. (Ord., 8-24-1974)
10-5-2: DENSITY REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Minimum lot width: Sixty feet (60').
   B.   Minimum lot area per family or dwelling unit:
      1.   Single-family: Seven thousand five hundred (7,500) square feet.
      2.   Two-family: Three thousand (3,000) square feet.
      3.   Multi-family: Two thousand five hundred (2,500) square feet.
   C.   Minimum required yards for the principal structure:
      1.   Front yard: Twenty five feet (25') or the average front yard setback
of the existing adjacent structures on both sides, but in no event with less
than twenty five feet (25') allowed or more than forty feet (40') required,
except for subdivisions having established setback lines shown on the plat.
Minimum front yard setbacks shall be required along all sides of the yard with
frontage along a street.
      2.   Side yards: Five feet (5').
      3.   Rear yard: Twenty feet (20'). (Ord., 8-24-1974)
10-5-3: NUMBER OF STRUCTURES PER LOT; PARKING:
   A.   Number Of Structures Per Lot: Only one principal structure allowed per
lot.
   B.   Parking: One off street parking space per dwelling unit. (Ord., 8-24-
1974)
10-5-4: PERMITTED USES:
Healthcare facilities excluding veterinarian facilities.
Professional, business and government offices.
Public and community facilities such as schools, places of worship, cemeteries,
libraries and recreation facilities.
Public utilities and service uses such as electric substations, gas regulator
stations, telephone transmission structures, pumping stations, transportation
facilities, etc.
Single-family dwellings not including mobile homes.
Two-family dwellings. (Ord., 10-13-1987; amd. 2010 Code)
10-5-5: ACCESSORY USES:
   A.   General Requirements:
      1.   Accessory structures shall be located only in the rear and side
yards.
      2.   Construction of the accessory buildings shall not precede
construction of the principal structure. (Ord., 8-24-1974)
   B.   Uses Enumerated:
Home occupation in a single-family dwelling; provided, that such use is
incidental to the main use of a dwelling, and further provided that the use is
limited to persons actually residing in the dwelling.
Private garage and storage building.
Satellite receiver dish antennas and microwave receiver dish antennas, subject
to site restrictions for said accessory uses in subsection
10-2-9L of this title.
Signs advertising premises for sale or rent. (Ord., 8-24-1974; amd. Ord., 12-
13-1988)
10-5-6: CONDITIONAL USES:
Funeral homes.
Mobile homes only in an approved mobile home park.
Multiple-family dwellings.
Publicly owned homes. (Ord., 8-24-1974)
CHAPTER 6
BUSINESS DISTRICTS
SECTION:
10-6-1: B-1 General Business District
10-6-2: B-2 Highway Business District
10-6-1: B-1 GENERAL BUSINESS DISTRICT:
   A.   Purpose: The general business district is established to provide areas
for a wide range of businesses as might be found in the central business
district.
   B.   Density Requirements:
      1.   Minimum lot width: None.
      2.   Minimum lot area: Two thousand five hundred (2,500) square feet.
      3.   Minimum required yards:
         a.   Front: None.
         b.   Side: None.
         c.   Rear: Twenty feet (20').
   C.   Parking: No off street parking is required. (Ord., 8-24-1974)
   D.   Permitted Uses:
All those uses permitted in the R-1 district.
Consumer services. Processing is permitted only if all such processing is
performed as a consumer service for customers served on the premises.
Motel, hotel restaurants.
Retail sales. Processing of products is permitted only if products are sold at
retail on the premises.
Single-family, two-family and multiple-family dwellings in conformance with the
minimum lot area, width and setbacks of the R-1 residential district. (Ord., 8-
24-1974; amd. 2010 Code)
   E.   Conditional Uses:
Light industry. (Ord., 8-24-1974)
   F.   Special Regulations:
      1.   All overhanging canopies, marquees, awnings and similar structures
must be at least eight feet (8') above a sidewalk at any point. Overhanging
signs must be a minimum of ten feet (10') above the sidewalk. Such structures
cannot project nearer than one foot (1') from any driveway or alley 1 . (Ord.,
8-24-1974; amd. 2010 Code)
      2.   Mobile homes are specifically excluded. (Ord., 8-24-1974)
 
Notes
  1. See also section
1 8-3-6 of this code and subsection
  10-2-9J of this title.
10-6-2: B-2 HIGHWAY BUSINESS DISTRICT:
   A.   Purpose And Location: The highway business district is established to
provide areas for the location of highway oriented businesses that require more
parking areas and street access. The highway business district shall include
all areas designated as such within the corporate limits of the city, and all
lands and waters within two hundred feet (200') of a federal or state highway
outside the corporate limits but within the jurisdictional areas of the city as
defined in section
10-2-7 of this title. (Ord., 12-23-1975)
   B.   Density Requirements:
      1.   Minimum lot size: Three thousand (3,000) square feet.
      2.   Minimum lot width: None.
      3.   Required yards:
         a.   Front: Twenty five feet (25') or the average front yard setback
of the existing adjacent structures on both sides, but in no event will less
than twenty five feet (25') be allowed, or more than forty feet (40') be
required.
         b.   Side: Ten feet (10').
         c.   Rear: Twenty feet (20').
   C.   Parking: One parking space (200 square feet) per two hundred (200)
square feet of gross commercial floor area. One parking space (200 square feet)
per four hundred (400) square feet of gross floor area for furniture, appliance
stores, motor vehicle sales, machinery sales, offices, etc. (Ord., 8-24-1974)
   D.   Permitted Uses:
      1.   Within the city limits, all those uses permitted in the B-1 district
except residential dwellings.
      2.   Outside the city limits but within the jurisdictional areas as
defined in section
10-2-7 of this title, all uses permitted in subsection D1 of this section, but
including residential dwellings when used in conjunction with agricultural
operations. (Ord., 12-23-1975)
   E.   Conditional Uses:
Residential dwellings.
   F.   Special Regulations: Sales services, processing and display may take
place outdoors. However, junkyards are not permitted. (Ord., 8-24-1974)
CHAPTER 7
MANUFACTURING DISTRICTS
SECTION:
10-7-1: M-1 Limited Manufacturing District
10-7-2: M-2 General Manufacturing District
10-7-1: M-1 LIMITED MANUFACTURING DISTRICT:
   A.   Purpose: The limited manufacturing district is created to provide
adequate desirable sites for industrial location and expansion that will not be
disruptive of existing or future residential areas.
   B.   Density Requirements:
      1.   Minimum lot size: None.
      2.   Minimum lot width: None.
      3.   Minimum yards:
         a.   Front: Twenty five feet (25') or the average front yard setback
on the existing adjacent structures on both sides, but in no event will less
than twenty five feet (25') be allowed, or more than forty feet (40') be
required.
         b.   Rear: Twenty feet (20').
         c.   Side: Fifteen feet (15').
   C.   Parking: One parking space (200 square feet) for each employee on the
maximum working shift, plus one for each vehicle used in the conduct of the
enterprise.
   D.   Permitted Uses:
Uses permitted in the B-1 business district, provided they comply with
regulations set forth in that district.
Industry, nonretail commercial, laboratory, offices, metal machining and
fabrication, production work.
   E.   Conditional Uses:
Residential dwelling units.
   F.   Special Regulations:
      1.   All processing shall take place within completely enclosed
buildings.
      2.   Storage auxiliary to the principal use is permitted in the open if
such storage activities occupy no more than twenty percent (20%) of the gross
lot area.
      3.   Screening shall be provided at lot boundaries abutting a residential
zoning district and shall consist of solid fencing or dense hedge or shrub to a
minimum of six feet (6') in height. (Ord., 8-24-1974)
10-7-2: M-2 GENERAL MANUFACTURING DISTRICT:
   A.   Purpose: The general manufacturing district is established to provide
areas in which manufacturing and related commercial operations are the
principal use of land. Such uses have some adverse effects on surrounding
properties and are not compatible with residential, institutional and retail
uses.
   B.   Density Requirements:
      1.   Minimum lot size: Ten thousand (10,000) square feet.
      2.   Minimum lot width: None.
      3.   Minimum yards:
         a.   Front: Twenty five feet (25').
         b.   Rear: Twenty feet (20').
         c.   Side: Fifteen feet (15').
      4.   Building height: Thirty five feet (35') or two (2) stories,
whichever is less.
   C.   Parking: One parking space (200 square feet) for each employee on the
maximum working shift, plus one for each vehicle used in the conduct of the
enterprise.
   D.   Permitted Uses:
Uses permitted in all other districts, provided they comply with regulations
set forth in their respective districts, except residential dwelling units
including mobile home parks.
Industry, nonretail commercial, laboratory, offices.
   E.   Conditional Uses:
Residential dwellings.
Slaughterhouses, fertilizer works, plants for the processing of animal skins or
hides and plants for the reduction of animal matter.
   F.   Special Regulations:
      1.   Processing and storage may take place within buildings, or outdoors
if screened properly from public view.
      2.   Screening shall be provided at lot boundaries abutting a residential
zoning district and shall consist of solid fencing or dense hedge or shrub to a
minimum of six feet (6') in height.
      3.   The following uses are prohibited: Crematories, fireworks or
explosive manufacture or storage, and dumping. (Ord., 8-24-1974)
CHAPTER 8
A-1 AGRICULTURAL DISTRICT
SECTION:
10-8-1: Purpose
10-8-2: Density Requirements
10-8-3: Accessory Uses
10-8-4: Conditional Uses
10-8-5: Special Regulations
10-8-6: Permitted Uses
10-8-1: PURPOSE:
The agricultural district is established to provide areas in which farming is
the principal use of the land. (Ord., 12-23-1975)
10-8-2: DENSITY REQUIREMENTS:
Same as for the R-1 residential district. (Ord., 12-23-1975)
10-8-3: ACCESSORY USES:
Same as for the R-1 residential district; except, that signs incidental to the
use of the occupied land may be erected. (Ord., 12-23-1975)
10-8-4: CONDITIONAL USES:
Light industry. (Ord., 12-23-1975)
10-8-5: SPECIAL REGULATIONS:
Junkyards, crematories, commercial feedlots, fireworks or explosives
manufacture or storage, mobile homes and mobile home parks are specifically
excluded. (Ord., 12-23-1975)
10-8-6: PERMITTED USES:
Municipal sewage treatment ponds and plants. (Ord., 12-23-1975)
CHAPTER 9
NONCONFORMING USES AND STRUCTURES
SECTION:
10-9-1: Nonconforming Structures
10-9-2: Nonconforming Uses
10-9-1: NONCONFORMING STRUCTURES:
   A.   Maintenance Permitted: A nonconforming structure lawfully existing on
the effective date hereof may be maintained except as otherwise provided in
this title.
   B.   Enlargement; Alteration: A nonconforming structure may not be enlarged
or structurally altered to an extent greater than fifty percent (50%) of the
square footage of ground area occupied by said structure. Such addition shall
conform to the use, height, yard and area requirements of the district in which
it is located.
   C.   Rebuilding: A nonconforming structure damaged by fire or other act of
God to an extent the owner feels is unrepairable may be replaced by a similar
new structure which shall not occupy, in square feet of ground area, an area
greater by fifty percent (50%) than the square footage of ground area occupied
by the destroyed or dismantled building. (Ord., 8-24-1974)
10-9-2: NONCONFORMING USES:
   A.   A nonconforming use lawfully existing on the effective date hereof may
be continued.
   B.   A nonconforming use may be changed only to a use of the same or more
restrictive classification.
   C.   A nonconforming use shall not be reestablished if discontinued for a
period of six (6) months or the property is sold. (Ord., 8-24-1974)
CHAPTER 10
ADMINISTRATION AND ENFORCEMENT
SECTION:
10-10-1: Administrative Officers
10-10-2: Zoning Administrator
10-10-3: Zoning Certificates
10-10-4: Occupancy Certificates
10-10-5: Appeals
10-10-1: ADMINISTRATIVE OFFICERS:
The administration of this title is hereby vested in the following officers of
the city:
   A.   The office of the zoning administrator.
   B.   The board of appeals 1 .
   C.   The office of the secretary of the board of appeals. (Ord., 8-24-1974)
 
Notes
1 1. See title 2, chapter 1 of this code.
10-10-2: ZONING ADMINISTRATOR:
   A.   Appointment: The zoning administrator shall be appointed by the mayor,
with the advice and consent of the city council.
   B.   Duties: The zoning administrator or his duly appointed and acting
assistant shall administer and enforce this title. It shall be the duty of the
zoning administrator to:
      1.   Receive and process applications for zoning certificates for
structures or additions thereto for which building permits are required.
      2.   Receive and process applications for zoning certificates not
accompanied by applications for building permits.
